1.0 SUMMARY 
 
J. Garry Clark of Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. has been retained by Discovery Harbour 
Resources Corp. ("Discovery") to review and evaluate its Wabassi Property in Northern 
Ontario (Figure 1).  The report is based on geologic, geophysical and geochemical data 
sets and diamond drill records supplied by Discovery, published literature and Ministry 
of Northern Development and Mines assessment files.  The author visited the property 
by helicopter on November 15th, 2012.  The helicopter flew from Thunder Bay and 
refuelled in Nakina.  During the visit the drill sites of holes 12WA-25, 26, 27 and 29 and 
12WA-31 and 32 of electromagnetic anomalies E and A2, respectively, were examined. 
 
This technical report is intended for use by Discovery Harbour Resource Corp. and CVC 
Cayman Ventures.  The purpose of this report is to satisfy the NI 43-101 requirements 
for a Reverse Take-Over (RTO) between Discovery Harbour and CVC Cayman 
Ventures, a publically-traded vehicle (V.CKV) on the Venture Exchange.  It describes 
and assesses the potential for intrusion-hosted nickel-copper deposits and volcanogenic 
massive sulphide (copper-zinc) deposits in the project area and provides 
recommendations including a work plan and budget for future exploration.  The report 
follows prescribed criteria and guidelines set forth by the Canadian Securities 
Association and described in National Instrument 43-101- Standards of Disclosure for 
Mineral Projects, Companion Policy 43-101CP and Form 43-101F1 (Technical Report).    
 
The mining claims that comprise the Wabassi Property are located 175 kilometres north 
of the town of Nakina, Ontario and approximately 54 km west of Marten Falls First 
Nation Community (Ogoki Post), Ontario.  The property is situated in the Ontario James 
Bay Lowlands area and within the National Topographic System (NTS) maps areas 
42M/10 and 42M/15.  The mining claims lie within the claim map areas of Nottik Island, 
Oxtoby Lake, Venton Lake, Saarimaki Lake, Wowchuk Lake and Gittins Lake in the 
Thunder Bay Mining Division, District of Thunder Bay North and Porcupine Mining 
Division, District of Cochrane.  The approximate UTM center point of the Wabassi 
property is: 526,500E / 5,731,500N (UTM, NAD 83, Zone 16).  The first claims were 
staked in the fall of 2007 but several were added until May 2011.  The Wabassi 
Property currently comprises 165 unpatented mining claim blocks, totalling 2,420 claim 
units (16 hectares per unit) covering 38720 hectares.   
 
The Property is accessible by floatplane and helicopter in the summer and by 
snowmobile or air in the winter.  The north portion of the Wabassi Property is also 
accessible by boat from the Martin Falls First Nation Community located 54 km to the 
west by navigating the Albany River and the Wabassi River but the latter can only be 
travelled as far west as Wabassi Falls, where the historical portage is no longer 
passable.  
 
The Property is in a remote location with scarce outcrop exposure.  The area has had 
little attention from government sponsored programs.  The principal map of the area 
was created from an Ontario Geological Survey project known as Operation Fort Hope.  
Operation Fort Hope covered a large area producing large scale maps.  Smaller scale 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 7 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

government maps do not exist in the area of the Property.  The area was also included 
in the Fort Hope Area geophysical program that provides a basic definition of the 
magnetic fabric of the eastern Uchi Domain. 
 
The only exploration completed on the Property (previously known as Wabassi Main 
and Wabassi North properties) has been by Northern Shield Resources Inc. after 
staking the property in 2007.  The work is described in detail in a technical report filed 
on www.sedar.com by Northern Shield Resources Inc. 
 
The Wabassi Property was originally owned 100% by Northern Shield Resources Inc. 
(Northern Shield) but optioned to Discovery Harbour on March 16, 2010. Discovery 
Harbour has now successfully earned a 51% interest in the property and has assumed 
operatorship.  The earn-in was completed approximately 9 months ahead of the 
scheduled date laid out in the option agreement. The terms of the option agreement are: 
 

(i) make an initial cash payment to Northern Shield of $50,000, (completed) 
(ii) purchase 800,000 Northern Shield shares at $0.25 per share for proceeds 

to Northern Shield of $200,000 (completed) 
(iii) fund $1,250,000 of exploration expenditures on the Property and issue to 

Northern Shield 100,000 common shares of Discovery on or before March 
31, 2011; and (completed) 

(iv) Fund an additional $2,150,000 million of exploration expenditures on the 
Property and issue to Northern Shield an additional 150,000 common 
shares of Discovery on or before March 31, 2012. (Expenditure 
completed, shares issuance completed and Joint Venture Agreement 
signed March 2012.) 
 

With Discovery having earning a 51% interest, a 51/49 joint venture to develop the 
Property is formed between Northern Shield and Discovery.  Discovery has earned the 
Operatorship and Northern Shield continues to manage the logistical aspects of the 
exploration and staffing of the project for a management fee of 5% of the expenditures, 
as more fully described in the Joint Venture section of the Option Agreement. 
 
A summary of the work completed on the Wabassi property follows: 
 

 Fall 2007, spring 2008 and summer 2009: prospecting, including reconnaissance 
mapping and sampling.  A total of 12 grab and 21 till samples were selected 
from the Wabassi Main area.  The grab samples were analysed for gold, 
platinum and palladium.  All but one sample did not exceed 10 ppb of either 
element. One sample 07WA-02, assayed 4 ppb gold, 25 ppb platinum and 105 
ppb palladium.  

 Assays and analyse of diamond drill core 08WA-02 (17 samples) and 08WA-04 
(91 samples).  All sample widths were less than 1.0 metre. The highest reported 
assay was from 08WA-04; 1.03 grams gold per tonne from 185.37 to 186.65 
metres. 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 8 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 A total of 5 core and 22 grab samples were sent for whole rock analysis and 
studied petrographically by Northern Shield. 

 Geotech Ltd. was contracted, in the fall of 2008, to complete a Versatile Time 
domain ElectroMagnetic (VTEM) helicopter electromagnetic and magnetic 
survey. The 150-metre line spaced survey defined the magnetic and 
electromagnetic characteristics of the property. 

 
Diamond drilling in the fall of 2008: Two diamond drill holes on the Wabassi North 
(08WA-01 (abandoned) + 08WA- 02 (175 metres)) andone diamond drill hole on the 
Wabassi Main (08WA-04 (347 metres)). 
 
The Wabassi Property is located within the Archean Sachigo Superterrane of the 
Superior Structural Province of the Canadian Shield. According to recent subdivisions of 
the Sachigo Superterrane, the Wabassi Intrusive Complex underlying the properties is 
located in the Uchi domain (2.8-2.9 Ga) of the North Caribou Terrane (Stott and Rayner, 
2004, Stott et al., 2007 and Stott, 2007a-b). However, the subdivisions are based mostly 
on work carried out on the western portion of the Sachigo Superterrane and since there 
is very little data available in the area of the properties, these boundaries remain highly 
speculative.  
 
There are a very limited number of outcrops in the area and they are restricted only to 
the most erosion-resistant lithologies. The outcrops observed in the area include quartz-
rich granitoids and metasediments and the most felsic and coarser grained 
gabbronorites from the Wabassi Complex. Because drilling is limited to specific areas of 
economic potential, the geological data obtained on drill core is minimally instructive, 
regarding regional geologic interpretations and lithologic associations with the exposed 
Archean to the west of the property. 
 
Until the recent discovery of volcanogenic massive sulphides in the bimodal volcanic 
rocks, the focus of exploration was the PGE and nickel-copper potential of the mafic-
ultramafic Wabassi Intrusive Complex, which is composed of the peridotitic Max 
Intrusion, the mafic-ultramafic layered Wabassi Main Intrusion (mainly composed of 
gabbronorite, olivine-gabbronorite, norite and local harzburgite) and the Wabassi North 
gabbroic intrusion. 
 
A significant portion of the Wabassi Property is underlain by the Wabassi Intrusive 
Complex, a large layered mafic ultramafic intrusion that is hosted within an Archean 
greenstone belt. Thus the intrusion has potential to host Ni-Cu-(PGE) mineralization 
which was the original objective when the property was staked in 2007. 
  
Drilling to date has identified two distinct rock types and styles of mineralization at 
Wabassi. Drilling in the A2 and E zones has intersected volcanic rocks and 
volcanogenic massive sulphide (VMS) copper-zinc-silver mineralization adjacent to the 
Wabassi Intrusive Complex. Drilling in the A1 zone has intersected lithologies 
predominantly consisting of mafic and ultramafic intrusives, belonging to the Wabassi 
Intrusive Complex. 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 9 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 
Discovery entered into an option agreement on the Wabassi Property with Northern 
Shield in March, 2010.  Work completed previous to the agreement is described within 
the Northern Shield Technical Report posted on Sedar (Vaillancourt and Bliss, 2010).  
Exploration completed from 2010 to present has resulted in the expansion of the 
property to the present size. 
 
The exploration completed includes: 
 
2010 

 13-hole diamond-drill program totalling of 3,100 metres 
 ground and borehole InfiniTEM surveys completed by Abitibi Geophysics 

coincident with the diamond drill program (17.3 line-kilometres and 4 diamond 
drill holes). 

 additional VTEM airborne geophysical surveys completed by Geotech Ltd. in 
2010 totalled 352 line kilometres @ 100 meter spacing & in 2011 totalled 3,845 
line kilometres @ 100 meter spacing 

 Detailed ground magnetics over the areas of Grid 1 
 
2011 

 surface and pulse EM survey completed by Crone Geophysics and Exploration 
Ltd.   

 Condor Consulting Ltd. was contracted to combine the 2008 and 2010 VTEM 
data and the 2010 InfiniTEM data to generate diamond drill targets 

 7 diamond drill holes totalling 2150 metres  
 Detailed ground magnetics over the areas of Grid 3 
 Contracted Jim Franklin of Franklin Geoscience to review core and other data to 

provide VMS setting and potential similarities to other typical deposits 
 2011 VTEM airborne geophysical survey over entire additional Wabassi Blocks 

 
2012 

 surface pulse EM surveys were completed by Crone Geophysics and Exploration 
Ltd. over regional targets #2-4 and # 2-9 from the 2011 Block 2 VTEM survey  

 A trial downhole DCIP (Earthprobe) survey was completed by Caracle Creek 
International Consulting over Anomaly E  

 Martin St. Pierre, consulting geophysicist, was contracted to interpret the Blocks 
2 and 3 VTEM data from the 2011 surveys and to generate diamond drill targets 

 12 diamond drill holes totalling 2,046 metres on regional targets 2-4 (2 holes, 111 
meters), 2-9 (2 holes, 337 meters), Anomaly E (4 holes, 966 meters), A1 Zone (2 
holes, 310 meters), A2 Zone (2 holes, 322 meters)  

 
 
 
A CDN $700,000.00 exploration budget is recommended to further assess the Wabassi 
Property for Volcanogenic massive sulphides and gold mineralization.  This exploration 
program is projected to span 12 to 14 months. 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 10 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 
Additional work programs and budgets will obviously be contingent on the results 
from this phase of exploration and because this is variable, any attempt to define 
objectives and specifics, regarding future activity and cost, would be speculative. It is 
the opinion of the author that the property is of sufficient merit to justify this proposed 
exploration. 
 
Given additional success in defining ore grade mineralization over significant widths, 
strike lengths and at depth at the A2 Zone and Anomaly E through diamond drilling, 
geochemistry and geophysics, it is not unreasonable to project a next phase of 
exploration requiring a budget of Cdn. $8 to $10 million, or more. 
 
The work completed to date has relied on quality geophysical surveys to allow the 
Discovery and Northern Shield geologists and their consultants to interpret the geology 
which is dominantly covered by glacial overburden. The success to date has proven the 
potential for significant volcanogenic massive sulphides (VMS) and shear zone-hosted 
gold mineralization.

2.0 INTRODUCTION 
 
J. Garry Clark of Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. has been retained by Discovery Harbour 
Resources Corp.  "Discovery" to review and evaluate its Wabassi Property in Northern 
Ontario (Figure 1).  The report is based on geologic, geophysical and geochemical data 
sets and diamond drill records supplied by Discovery, published literature and Ministry 
of Northern Development and Mines assessment files.  The author visited the property 
by helicopter on November 15th, 2012.  The helicopter flew from Thunder Bay and 
refuelled in Nakina.  During the visit the drill sites of holes 12WA-25, 26, 27 and 29 and 
12-WA31 and 32 of electromagnetic anomalies E and A2, respectively, were examined.   
 
This technical report is intended for use by Discovery Harbour Resource Corp and CVC 
Cayman Ventures. The purpose of this report is to satisfy the NI 43-101 requirements 
for a Reverse Take-Over (RTO) between Discovery Harbour and CVC Cayman 
Ventures, a publically-traded vehicle (V.CVK) on the TSX-Venture Exchange.  It 
describes and assesses the potential for intrusion-hosted nickel-copper deposits and 
volcanogenic massive sulphide (copper-zinc) deposits in the project area and provides 
recommendations including a work plan and budget for future exploration.  The report 
follows prescribed criteria and guidelines set forth by the Canadian Securities 
Association and described in National Instrument 43-101- Standards of Disclosure for 
Mineral Projects, Companion Policy 43-101CP and Form 43-101F1 (Technical Report).     
 
Discovery is a private company incorporated in accordance with the Business 
Corporations Act (British Columbia).  Discovery has entered into an option agreement 
with Northern Shield Resources "Northern Shield" and has now earned a 51% interest 
in the Wabassi Property. 
 
The author acknowledges the quality exploration and assistance from Christine 
Vaillancourt, Ian Bliss, Gabriela Budulan and Renee-Luce Simard of Northern Shield 
Resources Inc. Christine Vaillancourt provided excellent insight to the geology and 
geological setting of the Wabassi Property.

4.0 PROPERTY DESCRIPTION AND LOCATION 
 
The mining claims that comprise the Wabassi Property are located 175 kilometres north 
of the town of Nakina, Ontario and approximately 54 km west of Marten Falls First 
Nation Community (Ogoki Post), Ontario (Figure 2).  The property is situated in the 
Ontario James Bay Lowlands area and within the National Topographic System (NTS) 
maps areas 42M/10 and 42M/15.  The mining claims lie within the claim map areas of 
Nottik Island, Oxtoby Lake, Venton Lake, Saarimaki Lake, Wowchuk Lake and Gittins 
Lake in the Thunder Bay Mining Division, District of Thunder Bay North and Porcupine 
Mining Division, District of Cochrane.  The approximate UTM center point of the 
Wabassi property is: 526,500E / 5,731,500N (UTM, NAD 83, Zone 16).  The first claims 
were staked in the fall of 2007 but several were added until May 2011. The Wabassi 
Property currently comprises 165 unpatented mining claim blocks, totalling 2420 claim 
units (16 hectares per unit) covering 38,720 hectares (Figure 2, Table  1).

The claims have not been legally surveyed.  All claims are currently in good standing.  
The claims are recorded in the name of Discovery Harbour Resources Corp. (51%) and 
Northern Shield Resources Inc. (49%).  As the property comprises only staked claims 
there are no included surface rights: however,  a right to acquire the surface rights for 
development purposes exists through the Ontario Mining Act.  The Mining Act also 
provides legal access to the land for the purpose of exploration.  
 
The government of Ontario requires expenditures of $400 per year per unit, prior to 
expiry, to keep the claims in good standing for the following year.  The report must be 
submitted by the expiry date.  
 
There are no known environmental liabilities associated with the property.  For the 
proposed exploration program in this report no permits are required.  Permits are 
required if, during the course of exploration, waterways are affected.  The author does 
not know of any significant factors or risks that may affect access, title or the right or 
ability to perform work on the property. 
 
No mineral occurrence, resources, reserves or mine existing prior to the mineralization 
described in this report are known by the author to occur on the Property. 
 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 19 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

The property is located in the traditional lands of the Martin Falls First Nation.  Northern 
Shield and Discovery have been working with the First Nations community at Ogoki 
Post since 2004.  They have developed good working relationships with the community 
and the elders of the tribe. They have continuously kept the community informed of all 
activities within their area of influence, have worked with the community on projects and 
funding for activities for the youth of the community.

Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property

5.0 ACCESSIBILITY, CLIMATE, LOCAL RESOURCES, INFRASTRUCTURE AND 
PHYSIOGRAPHY 

 
The Property is accessible by floatplane and helicopter in the summer and by 
snowmobile or air in the winter. The north portion of the Wabassi Property is also 
accessible by boat from the Marten Falls First Nation Community by navigating the 
Albany River and the Wabassi River but the latter can only be travelled as far west as 
Wabassi Falls, where the historical portage is no longer passable.  
 
The claim area is mostly covered by an estimated 10-15 m thick sequence of glacial till 
with rare bedrock exposure. The highest elevation in the area of the properties is 220 m 
above sea level (a.s.l.) with an average elevation closer to 200 m above a.s.l. 
  
The area is characterized by low relief (less than 20 m) with a mixture of muskeg and 
mature spruce forests.  The claims are covered by typical northern boreal forest 
comprising spruce and jack pine.  Local fauna include moose, wolf, black bear, marten, 
hare and several species of birds. 
 
The climate is northern temperate, with warm summers and cold winters. Average 
monthly temperatures range from a maximum of 22°C in the summer to a minimum of  
-27°C in the winter.  Average annual precipitations are 462 mm of rain and 258 cm of 
snow for a total of 682 mm.  Exploration and development can be completed in all 
seasons. 
 
The land holdings are sufficient to allow for exploration and development.  The potential 
surface rights holdings, that can be triggered when the claims go to lease, are sufficient 
for development of infrastructure to sustain a mining operation. 
 
At present, there is no significant infrastructure in the area.  Sufficient skilled labour is 
present in Thunder Bay approximately 400 kilometres to the southwest and in the 
communities of Nakina, Hearst, Geraldton and Long Lac to the south.  The closest 
paved road and railway is approximately 170 kilometres to the south at Nakina.  
 
Recent discovery of significant chromite deposits has prompted the staking of a 
potential road, power and railway route from Nakina northward through the Wabassi 
property (see Figure 2).  Permits for the construction of this road have been applied for 
by Cliffs Natural Resources.  Cliffs Natural Resources and the Discovery-Northern 
Shield venture are presently in discussions to allow for Cliffs to gain access through the 
venture's claim group.  The venture would be allowed use of this road if these 
negotiations are completed as presently proposed.  
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 21 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

6.0 PROPERTY HISTORY 
 
The Wabassi Property was originally owned 100% by Northern Shield but under option 
by Discovery since March 16, 2010; Discovery has now earned a 51% interest in the 
property and has assumed operatorship.  The terms of the option agreement are: 
 

(i) make an initial cash payment to Northern Shield of $50,000, (completed) 
(ii) purchase 800,000 Northern Shield shares at $0.25 per share for proceeds 

to Northern Shield of $200,000 (completed) 
(iii) fund $1,250,000 of exploration expenditures on the Property and issue to 

Northern Shield 100,000 common shares of Discovery on or before March 
31, 2011; and (completed) 

(v) fund an additional $2,150,000 million of exploration expenditures on the 
Property and issue to Northern Shield an additional 150,000 common 
shares of Discovery on or before March 31, 2012. (expenditure 
completed, shares issuance completed and Joint Venture Agreement 
signed March 2012.) 
 

With Discovery having earning a 51% interest, a 51/49 joint venture to develop the 
Property is formed between Northern Shield and Discovery.  Discovery has earned the 
Operatorship and Northern Shield continues to manage the logistical aspects of the 
exploration and staffing of the project for a management fee of 5% of the expenditures, 
as more fully described in the Joint Venture section of the Option Agreement. 
 
The Property is in a remote location with scarce outcrop exposure.  The area has had 
little attention from government sponsored programs.  The principal map of the area 
was created from an Ontario Geological Survey project known as Operation Fort Hope 
(Thurston et al 1970).  Operation Fort Hope covered a large area producing large scale 
maps.  Smaller scale government maps do not exist in the area of the Property.  The 
area was also included in the Fort Hope Area geophysical program that provides a 
basic definition of the magnetic fabric of the eastern Uchi Domain (Ontario Geological 
Survey 2003). 
 
A review of the Ministry of Northern Development and Mines assessment records 
indicates no exploration for Ni-Cu-(PGE) or volcanogenic massive sulphides exploration 
has been completed in the area prior to Northern Shield's acquisition of the property. 
 
An area to the north of the property had been targeted by Kerr Addison Mines Ltd.  Kerr 
Addison completed an airborne survey in 1980 with a limited follow up diamond drill 
program in 1983.  The program evaluated the airborne electromagnetic anomalies and 
reported various metavolcanic units. No assays were reported in the diamond drill logs 
filed for assessment with the government. 
 
The only exploration completed on the Property (previously known as Wabassi Main 
and Wabassi North properties) has been by Northern Shield after staking the property in 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 22 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

2007.  The work is described in detail in a technical report filed on www.sedar.com by 
Northern Shield (Vaillancourt and Bliss). 
 
The following summarizes the work completed on the Wabassi property: 
 

 Fall 2007, spring 2008 and summer 2009: prospecting, including reconnaissance 
mapping and sampling.  A total of 12 grab and 21 till samples were selected 
from the Wabassi Main area.  The grab samples were analysed for gold, 
platinum and palladium. All but one sample did not exceed 10 ppb of either 
element. One sample 07WA-02 assayed 4 ppb gold, 25 ppb platinum and 105 
ppb palladium.  

 Assays and analyses of diamond drill core 08WA-02 (17 samples) and 08WA-04 
(91 samples).  All sample widths were less than 1.0 metres. The highest 
reported assay was from 08WA-04; 1.03 grams gold per tonne from 185.37 to 
186.65 metres (Figure 3). 

 A total of 5 core and 22 grab samples were sent for whole rock analysis and 
studied petrographically by Northern Shield. 

 Geotech Ltd. was contracted, in the fall of 2008, to complete a Versatile Time 
domain ElectroMagnetic (VTEM) helicopter electromagnetic and magnetic 
survey. The 150 metre line spaced survey defined the magnetic and 
electromagnetic characteristics of the property (Figure 4). 

 Diamond drilling in the fall of 2008: Two diamond drill holes on the Wabassi 
North (08WA-01 (abandoned) + 08WA- 02 (175 metres)). One diamond drill hole 
on the Wabassi Main intrusion (08WA-04 (347 metres) Figure 3).   

 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 23 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 
Figure 3: Location of Historical Drilling, Grab Sampling and Till Sampling  (Vaillancourt and Bliss, 2010)  

 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 24 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 
Figure 4: Interpretation of 2008 VTEM Survey  (Vaillancourt and Bliss, 2010) 

 
Diamond drill hole 08WA-04 was designed to test a VTEM conductor and was drilled on 
the western edge of the main Wabassi intrusion (A2 Zone) The lithologies intercepted 
were mainly composed of cumulate-textured gabbronorite and possibly olivine-
gabbronorite, similar to those sampled on surface. Pyrite / pyrrhotite intersected in this 
hole appear to explain the EM anomaly that was targeted.  
 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 25 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

Diamond drill hole 08WA-01 drilled at Wabassi North intersected a medium-grained 
granite but was abandoned after just under 15 metres and the drill had to be moved 
because of lack of water supply. Diamond drill hole 08WA-02 intersected a variety of 
gabbros and hornblende-gabbros, which are intruded by several granitic dikes from a 
depth of approximately 112 metres. These gabbros alternately displayed a variety of 
textures including ophitic to sub-ophitic, granoblastic and pegmatoidal. 
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 26 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

7.0 GEOLOGICAL SETTING AND MINERALIZATION 
 
7.1 Regional Geology 
 
The Wabassi Property is located within the Archean Sachigo Superterrane of the 
Superior Structural Province of the Canadian Shield. According to recent subdivisions of 
the Sachigo Superterrane (Figure 5), the Wabassi Intrusive Complex underlying the 
properties is located in the Uchi domain (2.8-2.9 Ga) of the North Caribou Terrane (Stott 
and Rayner, 2004, Stott et al., 2007 and Stott, 2007a-b). However, the subdivisions are 
based mostly on work carried out on the western portion of the Sachigo Superterrane 
and since there is very little data available in the area of the properties, these 
boundaries remain highly speculative.  
 

 
Figure 5: Regional Geology (after Stott et al. 2007). 

 
 
 
 
 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 27 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

7.2 Local and Property Geology 
 
7.2.1 Introduction 
 
There are a very limited number of outcrops in the area and they are restricted only to 
the most erosion-resistant lithologies. The outcrops observed in the area include quartz-
rich granitoids and metasediments and the most felsic and coarser grained 
gabbronorites from the Wabassi intrusion. Because drilling is limited to specific areas of 
economic potential, the geological data obtained on drill core is minimally instructive, 
regarding regional geologic interpretations and lithologic associations with the exposed 
Archean to the west of the property. 
 
Until the recent discovery of volcanogenic massive sulphides in the bimodal volcanic 
rocks, the focus of exploration was the PGE and nickel-copper potential of the mafic-
ultramafic Wabassi Intrusive Complex, which is composed of the peridotitic Max 
Intrusion, the mafic-ultramafic layered Wabassi Intrusion (mainly composed of 
gabbronorite, olivine-gabbronorite, norite and local harzburgite) and the Wabassi North 
gabbroic intrusion. 
 
The Wabassi intrusive Complex (including the ultramafic rocks underlying the Max 
Property) is hosted mostly by an unnamed assemblage of mafic, intermediate and felsic 
volcanic rocks that is likely the continuation of the Miminiska-Fort Hope Archean 
greenstone belt. Units observed in core to date include: blue quartz porphyritic rhyolite; 
feldspar +/- quartz porphyritic intermediate fragmental volcanic rocks of dacitic to 
andesitic compositions with related porphyry dikes; intermediate tuff and lapilli tuff; and 
a mafic to ultramafic amphibole porphyritic flow. Zinc-rich massive sulphide of 
volcanogenic origin was intersected between the felsic porphyritic and intermediate 
volcanic sequences. The volcanic rocks and the sulphide mineralization are described 
in more detail in section 9 of this report. 
 
The mafic-ultramafic Wabassi Complex and host volcanic rocks are also in contact with 
granitoids from the foliated tonalitic suite to the north and from the massive granodiorite 
to granite suite to the southeast, both also observed in core. 
 
7.2.2 Wabassi Intrusive Complex 
 
The Wabassi complex is composed of the Max ultramafic intrusion to the west, the 
Wabassi mafic-ultramafic intrusion to the east and the Wabassi North gabbro. The 
magnetic fabric displayed on the airborne survey shows the outline of the three bodies 
very well. 
 
The Wabassi Intrusive Complex mostly shows very little to no penetrative deformation 
and the primary textures are very well preserved, particularly in the mafic portions. This 
initially suggested a Proterozoic age. However, Archean age mafic-ultramafic intrusions 
may be very well preserved, particularly if they are surrounded by softer rocks that will 
take most of the effect of strain caused by tectonic activity, and preserve the solid mafic 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 28 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

intrusion. A small isotopic study carried on 2 samples from the Max intrusion and one 
from the Wabassi intrusion suggests Archean ages both for the Max and the Wabassi 
portion but the results are somewhat equivocal and more samples need to be analysed 
to validate the geochronology. 
 
The main Wabassi mafic-ultramafic intrusion includes a variety of cumulate lithologies 
composed of variable amounts of olivine, plagioclase, orthopyroxene, clinopyroxene 
and hornblende as cumulate, oikocryst or interstitial. Other interstitial and alteration 
minerals commonly found are magnetite, actinolite, biotite, chlorite, epidote and 
carbonate. Harzburgite and lherzolite were intersected in core near the western contact 
but most of the extent of the Wabassi Intrusion appears to be mafic and composed 
principally of olivine-gabbronorite and gabbronorite with subordinate norite, troctolite 
and gabbro. Although the very well preserved cumulate textures and the large scale 
magnetic signature suggest a layered intrusion, very limited small scale layering was 
clearly observed to date. These data do not preclude that the intrusion is layered, but 
simply that it isn't commonly observed, which could be the result of two things: 1) 
gabbronorite olivine-gabbronorite are the only units outcropping, possibly because they 
are the most erosion-resistant, and 2) information from drilling comes almost exclusively 
from the western edge of the intrusion, where the EM anomalies are located. The edge 
of the intrusion has suffered the effects of deformation and also alteration due to cross-
cutting dikes much more than the core of the intrusion and original textures and 
structures may be more difficult to discern. 
 
Gabbros and hornblende-gabbro were observed and sampled throughout the Main 
Wabassi intrusion and the Wabassi North gabbro intrusion. These vary in texture from 
cumulate (likely part of the same magmatic event as the gabbronorites and olivine-
bearing units describe above) to intergranular or sub-ophitic (could be late phases 
associated with the cumulate units or cross-cutting dikes of a different event). 
 
Metavolcanic Rocks 
 
Prior to drilling by Northern Shield, there was little information available about the 
volcanic rocks underlying the Wabassi and Max properties. These include a small 
number of mafic volcanic outcrops reported on the Operation Fort Hope, Attawapiskat 
River Sheet map (Thurston and Carter, 1970) to the west of the Wabassi Property. It is 
generally assumed that these volcanic rocks are the continuation of the Miminiska-Fort 
Hope belt, better known to the west of the Property area and where a new mapping 
program by the Ontario Geological Survey is currently underway. 
 
To date, the volcanic rocks intersected in core can be roughly divided in 3 distinct 
packages: 1) Ultramafic, mostly massive and amphibole porphyritic; 2) mafic massive 
flows and breccias, commonly variolitic; 3) Felsic, rhyolitic to dacitic, largely blue-quartz 
porphyritic, quartz-feldspar porphyritic or feldspar porphyritic. 
 
The ultramafic assemblage was intersected in holes 11WA-16, 11WA-19 and 12WA-28 
(Figure 12). It is currently interpreted to be volcanic or shallow intrusive but requires 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 29 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

much more study to be able to determine its nature. No textures common to ultramafic 
flows were observed in core (spinifex) but this unit is very carbonate altered. It typically 
displays large 3-4 mm amphibole phenocrysts.  Olivine is preserved in one of the only 
two samples processed for lithogeochemistry and petrography. 
 
The mafic metavolcanic assemblages are of basaltic to andesitic composition.  It is 
generally very altered and pale green, which makes it difficult to distinguish from the 
felsic metavolcanic that is not quartz-phyric. Although not commonly reported in the 
logs, these rocks generally contain small amphibole phenocrysts visible in thin section. 
Their geochemistry is clearly distinct from the felsic metavolcanic rocks with lower silica 
content, significantly higher titanium and iron, and lower abundances of incompatible 
trace elements such as rare-earth elements. Varioles, which were logged mostly as 
fragments but later reinterpreted, are a common and a very characteristic feature in 
these mafic rocks. No pillow selvages were observed in core to date. 
 
The felsic metavolcanic rocks vary in composition between rhyolite and dacite and a 
large proportion of these lithologies display blue quartz eyes up to about 5 mm in size. 
They are generally massive flows, fragmentals and breccias. The volcanogenic massive 
sulphides encountered to date are mostly contained within or just above this 
assemblage of felsic metavolcanic rocks.  
 
The volcanic rocks are metamorphosed to the upper greenschist to lower amphibolite 
facies in general but no thorough metamorphic study was carried to date. Additional 
lithogeochemistry and petrography studies are currently underway. These results will 
help significantly with the understanding of the stratigraphy, petrology and metamorphic 
grade determination. Structural deformation, in general, is unusually low compared to 
other better known greenstone belts in the Superior Province. Most of the metavolcanic 
or intrusive rocks show little to no sign of penetrative fabric and the primary textures are 
well preserved unless the rock is very altered. Schistosity is locally developed but 
generally weak and over small intervals only, as narrow shear zones. 
 
 

  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 30 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

7.3 Mineralization 
 
A significant portion of the Wabassi Property is underlain by the Wabassi Intrusive 
Complex, a large layered mafic ultramafic intrusion that is hosted within an Archean 
greenstone belt. Thus the intrusion has potential to host Ni-Cu-(PGE) mineralization 
which was the original objective when the property was staked in 2007. 
  
Drilling to date has identified rock types common to typical VMS systems, across 
Canada and worldwide, along with typical styles of VMS and shear-zone hosted gold 
mineralization at Wabassi. Drilling in the A2 and E zones (Figure 12) has intersected 
volcanic rocks and volcanogenic massive sulphide (VMS) copper-zinc-silver 
mineralization adjacent to the Wabassi Intrusive Complex. Lithologies predominantly 
consisting of mafic and ultramafic intrusives, belonging to the Wabassi Intrusive 
Complex were intersected at the A1 Zone.  Also in the A1 Zone, DDH 12WA-30 
intersected a quartz-carbonate-pyritic shear zone. This was a heterolithic breccia with a 
quartz-carbonate matrix at 130.9 meters to 148.9 meters (18 meters).  A strongly 
altered and silicified zone was intercected from 134.5 to 137.6 meters (3.1 meters).  
Gold mineralization occurs within this 3.1 meter zone and averages 5.9 g/t Au (0.19 opt 
Au).  Within this 3.1 meter zone, a 1.03 meter interval (135.52 to 136.55 meters) 
reported 16.3 g/t Au (0.51 opt Au). 
 
The A2 Zone is exemplified by drill-hole 10WA-07 that intersected 2.25% zinc, 31.7 g/t 
silver and 0.17% copper over 49.5 meters, including a higher grade section of 7.07% Zn 
over 7 meters. Three sample intervals from this drill-hole also contained over 100 g/t 
silver including a 0.7 meter interval grading 536 g/t silver (15.63 oz/ton) and three other 
intervals contained over 12% Zn. 
  
Four kilometres to the south of the A2 Zone, drill-holes 11WA-16 and 17 intersected 
VMS–type mineralization at Anomaly E.  Significant results from drill-hole 11WA-16 
include 1.1 % Cu, 2.3% Zn, 54 g/t Ag and 0.14 g/t Au over 20.05 meters, which included  
higher grade sections of 1.5% Cu, 3.3% Zn, 76 g/t Ag and 0.2 g/t Au over 13.1 meters 
and 1.7% Cu, 4.5% Zn and 91 g/t Ag over 7.7 meters. Hole 11WA-17, located 100 
meters along strike from 11WA-16, intersected 1.4% Cu, 2.1% Zn, 34 g/t Ag and 0.1 g/t 
Au over 30.64 meters, which included a higher grade section of 2.6% Cu, 4.8% Zn, 66 
g/t Ag and 0.2 g/t Au over 12.7 meters and 5.7% Cu, 9.9% Zn and 150 g/t Ag and 0.33 
g/t Au over 3.6 meters.  Grades of up to 9.1% copper, 25.5% zinc and 217 g/t silver 
over 1.0 metre core lengths were intersected in this drill-hole.  The 2012 diamond 
drilling program (see Section 10: Diamond Drilling) continued to support the high grade 
nature of mineralization within the E Zone.  Multiple new intercepts from 2012 drilling at 
Anomaly E continue to exhibit ore grade intercepts of copper, zinc and silver (see 
Section 10: Diamond Drilling). 
  
Drill-holes in the A1 Zone dominantly intersected pyrrhotite-dominated massive, semi-
massive and disseminated and net-textured sulphides containing copper, silver, and 
zinc and nickel mineralization.  Eighty-five of the one hundred and thirty-four samples 
assayed from drill-hole 10WA-05 assayed greater than 5 g/t silver.  The assays results, 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 31 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

mineralogy and textures suggest the A1 Anomaly may be the result of hybrid mixing of 
VMS and magmatic systems. 
 
The amount of drilling to date is insufficient to determine the length, width, depth and 
continuity of the mineralization. Significantly more drilling will be required. All 
mineralized intercepts to date, are core length as true thicknesses have not been 
determined. 
 
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 32 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

8.0 DEPOSIT TYPES 
 
8.1 PGE and Ni-Cu-PGE (written by Christine Vaillancourt & Ian Bliss / Northern 
Shield) 
 
The following section (8.1only)  is taken from an NI 43-101 technical report written by 
Christine Vaillancourt and Ian Bliss for Northern Shield Resources Inc. dated March 5th, 
2010 and filed on SEDAR on August 27th, 2010 by Northern Shield Resources Inc. 
 
"The Wabassi and Wabassi North properties were staked by Northern Shield based on 
the geophysical pattern observed on the magnetic survey published by the Ontario 
Geological Survey (OGS) in the Fort Hope area (Ontario Geological Survey, 2003), 
which suggests a layered intrusion.  Limited field observations and sampling confirmed 
the presence of cumulate gabbro, gabbronorites and olivine-gabbronorites, along with 
local layering at the scale of the outcrop.  These observations confirmed that at least 
part of the Wabassi intrusive complex is a layered mafic to possibly ultramafic intrusion. 
The anomalous values of Pt and Pd (130 ppb Pt+Pd) found in one of the 3 samples 
analysed from the first sample collection in 2007 also confirmed the potential for PGE 
and/or Ni-Cu-(PGE) deposits in the intrusive complex.  Based on work carried out to 
date, the ultramafic rocks found by diamond drilling underlying the Max property to the 
west (Joint Venture between Northern Shield and Rainy Mountain Capital Corp.) are 
currently interpreted to be related to the main Wabassi layered complex.  Further 
petrographic, geochemical and possibly geochronology and other isotope studies will be 
required to confirm or rule out the association between the two bodies.  One diamond-
drill hole from the Wabassi North Property revealed the presence of a variety of 
gabbros.  Their relationship with the gabbronorites and olivine-gabbronorites on the 
main Wabassi Property cannot be confirmed at this time because of insufficient data. 
 
The association between mafic rocks observed in the field and a well-layered 
stratigraphy, as interpreted from airborne magnetic fabrics and field observations, 
suggested the potential for a large layered intrusion that could host "reef-style" PGE 
mineralization similar to that occurring in the Bushveld Igneous Complex (South Africa) 
or the Stillwater Complex (Montana, USA)." 
 
 
8.2 Volcanogenic Massive Sulphide 
 
8.2.1 Introduction 
 
Volcanogenic massive sulphide (VMS) deposits are significant producers of Zn, Cu, Pb, 
Ag and Au globally, and may contain a number of associated elements including Co, 
Sn, Cd, In, Bi, Se, Mn, Te, Ga, Ge ± As, Sb and Hg (Lydon, 1988, Misra, 2000, Galley 
et al., 2007). VMS deposits are a class of hydrothermal ore deposits which typically 
occur as lenses of polymetallic massive sulphide that form at or near the seafloor in 
submarine volcanic environments from metal-enriched fluids associated with seafloor 
hydrothermal convection (Galley et al., 2007). Deposits range in age from Archean to 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 33 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

actively forming deposits in modern seafloor spreading and oceanic arc terranes 
(Lydon, 1988, Misra, 2008; Galley et al., 2007).  
 
 
8.2.2 Formation 
 
The six components required for the formation of VMS deposits in a hydrothermal 
system are: 1) a heat source (subvolcanic intrusion) driving the hydrothermal system; 2) 
a water-rock interaction zone; 3) fracture/fault zones allowing fluid flow; 4) footwall 
and/or hanging-wall alteration zones; 5) VMS deposit(s); and 6) distal products of 
chemical precipitation of sediment in the water column (Figure 6). This model also 
shows that at different stages in the hydrothermal system, some elements are gained 
while other are lost. Semi conformable alteration zones (distal to VMS deposits) show 
increases in Ca-Si-Fe-Na-K-Mg (epidotization-silicification, actinolite-clinozoisite-
magnetite, spilitization, and chlorite-sericite±K-feldspar alteration assemblages). 
Stockwork vein systems (proximal alteration assemblages) show increases in Fe and 
Mg and depletion in Na, Ca and Si reflecting feldspar destruction (chlorite-quartz–
sulphide or sericite-quartz-pyrite±aluminosilicate-rich alteration assemblages; Galley et 
al., 2007 and Lydon, 1988). The zone overlying subvolcanic intrusions can be altered to 
amphibolite-facies assemblages followed by Na-Ca-rich greenschist-facies 
assemblages. Subsequently and in close proximity to the seafloor zeolite-clay, 
carbonates and sub-greenschist mineral assemblages are found (Galley et al., 2007).

8.2.4 Mineralogy 
 
The massive ore zone of VMS deposits is composed dominantly of chalcopyrite, 
sphalerite, galena, pyrite and pyrrhotite. Additional accessory ore and silicate minerals 
found within the massive sulphide lens and alteration zone in minor to trace quantities, 
compiled from a variety of VMS deposits include arsenopyrite, bornite, cassiterite, 
magnetite, Au-bearing minerals, Ag-bearing minerals, Bi-bearing minerals, Co-As 
sulphides, Cu-Sn sulphides, selenides, tellurides, tennantite, chalcocite, covelite, 
digenite, scheelite, molybdenite, ilmenite, rutile, and marcasite (Dube et al., 2007; 
Hannington et al., 1999; Misra, 2000; Lydon, 1988; Franklin et al., 2005; Galley et al., 
2007; Huston et al., 1995, 1996; Peter et al., 2003; Slack et al., 2003, 2005; Grant, 
2009).  
 
8.2.5 Classification Schemes 
 
Several classification schemes have been proposed for VMS deposits over the last few 
decades. The two most common classification schemes are those suggested by Large 
(1992), Franklin et al. (1981), Franklin (1993), Barrie and Hannington (1999), and 
Franklin et al. (2005) based on 1) major ore-element chemistry and 2) lithostratigraphy 
and tectonic setting.  
 
The most common and simpler classification is divisible into two groups: 1) Cu-Zn, 
hosted mostly but not exclusively by mafic volcanic rocks; and 2) Zn-Pb-Cu, hosted 
largely by felsic volcanic rocks. There are several mineralogical and compositional 
differences between the two groups such as the Zn-Pb-Cu group relative to the Cu-Zn 
group displaying a higher Pb:(Zn+Pb) ratio, lower Au:Ag ratio, differences in gangue 
mineralogy, more pronounced sericite alteration and higher δ34S values (Lydon, 1988; 
Misra, 2000). The VMS mineralisation intersected to date on the Wabassi Property 
appears to relate to the Cu-Zn type. 
 
The second classification system presented by Barrie and Hannington (1999) and 
Franklin et al. (2005) separates VMS deposits into six different groups (Fig. 3): 1) 
bimodal-mafic; 2) mafic; 3) pelite-mafic; 4) bimodal-felsic; 5) siliciclastic-felsic; and 6) 
hybrid bimodal felsic. Massive ore, stockwork and alteration mineralogy of VMS 
deposits defined by Franklin et al. (2005) is summarized in Table 6 and graphically 
represented in Figure 8.

9.0 EXPLORATION  
 
Discovery entered into an option agreement on the Wabassi Property with Northern 
Shield in March, 2010.  Work completed previous to the agreement is described in 
Section 6 Property History and within the Northern Shield Technical Report posted on 
Sedar (Vaillancourt and Bliss, 2010).  Exploration completed from 2010 to present has 
resulted in the expansion of the property to the present size (Figure 9 and 10). 
 
The exploration completed includes: 

2010 
 13-hole diamond-drill program totalling of 3,100 metres 
 ground and borehole InfiniTEM surveys completed by Abitibi Geophysics 

coincident with the diamond drill program (17.3 line-kilometres and 4 diamond 
drill holes). 

 additional VTEM airborne geophysical survey completed by Geotech Ltd. in 2010 
totalled 352 line kilometres @ 100 meter

9.1 Geophysical Surveying  
 
9.1.1 Airborne Geophysical Surveys 
 
Helicopter-borne versatile time domain electromagnetic (VTEM) geophysical surveys, 
performed by Geotech, were completed in 2008, 2010 and 2011 to cover various parts 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 39 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

of the Wabassi property.  The areas covered by VTEM surveys are illustrated in Figures 
9 and 11. 
 
The 2008 VTEM survey interpretation is presented in Section 6 Property History (Figure 
4). 
 
The area of the 2010 Wabassi West VTEM survey is interpreted to be underlain by the 
Wabassi Intrusive Complex. This survey identified two extensions of the 2008 VTEM 
survey anomalies and one new anomaly (Figure 10).  Anomaly "C" from the 2008 
survey has been defined to extend ~ 1000 metres to the west –southwest.  Anomaly 
"A3", from the 2008 survey is also extended to the south ~ 600 metres.  The newly 
identified anomaly "E" is located within the centre of the survey.  Anomaly "E" has very 
strong conductance and can be traced on 5 lines. 
 

The 2011 VTEM survey was designed to evaluate the additional land holding described 
as Block 2 and 3 (Geotech 2011) (Figure 11).  The total area coverage is 394 km2. Total 
survey line coverage is 4397.0 line kilometres. The principal sensors included a Time 
Domain EM system and a magnetometer.  Flight lines were spaced at 100 metres with 
tie lines every 1000 metres.  The helicopter mean altitude was 72 metres for the two 
blocks.

9.2 Ground and Downhole Geophysics 
 
9.2.1 Surface and Borehole InfiniTEM Survey by Abitibi Geophysics 
 
A geophysical time domain electromagnetic (TDEM) program utilizing the InfiniTEM 
configuration (surface 17.3 km and 4 boreholes) was complete by Abitibi Geophysics in 
March 2010. Two separate grids were originally planned, one located in the southern 
part of the property and partly covering Venton Lake (Grid 1) and one on the west side 
of the intrusion (Grid 2), where the "A" series of EM anomalies are located (Figure 9 and 
10). Due to an earlier spring melt Grid 1 and diamond drill hole 10WA-01 were not 
accessible when the survey crew arrived.  On Grid 2, ground readings from lines 0+00S 
to 23+00S were recorded.  Lines 23+00S to 33+00S were not surveyed due the early 
melt.  Diamond drill holes 10WA-04, 10WA-05, 10WA-06 and 10WA-07 were 
completed. 
 
9.2.2 Surface and Borehole Pulse EM Surveys by Crone Geophysics and 
Exploration Ltd. 
 
A TDEM survey was carried out by Crone Geophysics and Exploration Ltd. in February 
and March 2011 on three separate grids on the Wabassi Property (Figure 9).  A total of 
22 lines covering four surface loops (three on Grid 1 (10.5 line-kms) and one on Grid 3 
(4.2 line-kms), and four holes (on Grid 2, 10WA – 8,9,10 & 11) were surveyed. 
However, DDH 10WA-08 was blocked and unable to be surveyed.  
 
9.2.3 Ground Magnetics 
 
A very high-resolution ground magnetic survey was completed on portions of Grid 1 
covering Anomalies A1 and A2 in 2010. Over the A1 Zone, readings were taken every 5 
seconds along 25 meter spaced grid lines. At A2, magnetic readings were taken at 10 
metre stations on 50 metre spaced lines (Figure 9).  Grid 3 was completed in 2011 
(Figure 9). The program was useful at defining the geology in the areas of the 
anomalies.   
 
9.2.4 Trial EarthProbe Borehole DCIP survey of 11WA-17 & 11WA-20 
 
At the request of Northern Shield Resources Inc. and Discovery Harbour Resources, 
Caracle Creek International Consulting Inc. (Caracle Creek) was commissioned to 
undertake an EarthProbe borehole resistivity and induced polarization (DCIP) survey at 
the Wabassi Property.  The objective of the survey was to determine the extent and 
orientation of mineralized intersections identified during diamond drilling (to the extent 
possible) and determine if additional off-hole targets exist.  The geophysical survey was 
undertaken from February 6 – 12, 2012 using the EarthProbe high resolution DCIP 
system.  The system can be configured for the collection of high resolution surface IP 
data, single borehole vertical profiles (VP), and/or multi-bore/surface-to-bore 
tomographic images.  For this survey, data were collected using single borehole vertical 
profiling and borehole-to-borehole tomographic imaging.  The scope of work was to 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 44 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

comprise VP and tomographic imaging of 4 boreholes (11WA-16, 11WA-17, 11WA-19 
and 11WA-20).  Holes 11WA-16 and 11WA-19 were attempted but were blocked near 
surface and unable to be imaged.  
 
Results of the vertical profiling and borehole-to-borehole imaging from 11WA-17 and 
11WA-20 using the EarthProbe high resolution borehole DCIP system has shown: 
 

 Mineralized zones within the area tested exhibit a low resistivity (less than 300 
Ohm.m); high chargeability is not definitively associated with the mineralized 
zones. 

 The narrow electrode separation of the EarthProbe system can detect 
mineralized regions as narrow as 3 m (narrower zones untested).  

 The mineralization intersected in 11WA-17 between 254.86 and 285.50 m 
extends at least 40 m off-hole. 

 Two zones of low resistivity and high chargeability were identified off-hole of 
11WA-17 at 100 – 140 m depth (35 m off-hole) and 160 – 190 m depth (40 m off-
hole). 

 One zone of low resistivity/high chargeability was detected off-hole of 11WA-20 
(180 – 280 m depth and approximately 60 m off-hole). 

 
Based on these limited results borehole DCIP, in particular resistivity appears to be a 
valuable tool for delineating the extent of Cu-Zn, Ag-Au mineralization at Anomaly E.  
With more data, 3D inversion of the vertical profiling and tomography data will enhance 
the spatial understanding of features of interest within the exploration area.  
Additionally, a larger dataset will facilitate enhanced understanding of the DCIP 
signature of the lithologic units present in the project area. 
 
9.3. Discussion of Geophysics 
 

9.3.1 2008, 2010 and 2011 Geophysics 
 
The 2010 drill program was designed to test a series of VTEM anomalies identified from 
the 2008 survey.  The details of the diamond drill programs are described in Section 10: 
Diamond Drilling.  These VTEM anomalies are identified as Targets "A" through "E." 
(Figure 12).  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 45 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 

Figure 12: The Wabassi Intrusion with location of 2008 and 2010 Wabassi VTEM anomalies  and drill holes. 

(Internal Northern Shield Resources Inc. 2012) 
 
The "A" group anomalies are located along a strong linear magnetic feature on the 
western edge of the Wabassi Intrusion.  The anomalies were interpreted to be possible 
Ni-Cu-(PGE) massive sulphides at the contact of the intrusion. 
 
The A1 anomaly can be traced clearly over three flight lines (lines 4400, 4410, 4420) at 
150 meters spacing for a strike length of at least 300 meters.  An EM signature is also 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 46 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

seen on lines 4390, 4380 and 4370 but the interpretation of this is ambiguous.  One 
possible interpretation is that the signature is caused by the highly magnetic layer being 
closer to the receiver because lines 4370 to 4390 cross a topographic ridge in this area.  
The second possible interpretation is that the conductor under this portion is the same 
as those on lines 4400 to 4420 but at greater depth.  Either interpretation strongly 
suggests the presence of a fault between lines 4390 and 4400. 
 
Anomaly A2 is located on line 4460 and on tie-line 4780, though a subtle signature is 
also seen on line 4450.  This is the strongest VTEM signature so far identified on the 
property.  This anomaly was targeted in 2008 with drill-hole 08WA-04 but was not 
explained.  Subsequent drilling of holes 10WA-07 & 13 later revealed that hole 08WA-
04 had undercut the conductor which is caused by VMS style mineralization. 
 
The A3 anomaly is located on line 4500 on the very edge of the 2008 VTEM survey.  It 
was expanded to the south by the Wabassi West 2010 VTEM survey.  The A3 
conductor, along with the A4 conductor has not been drill tested to date. 
 
Anomaly B is a moderate conductor located on the eastern edge of the Wabassi 
Intrusion and is coincident with an isolated magnetic high.  This target was tested with 
drill-hole 10WA-02. The conductor was not explained with this drill hole. 
 
Anomaly C was detected on the very south west corner of the 2008 VTEM survey and 
was unsuccessfully tested in 2010 with drill-hole 10WA-01.  The ground grid #1 was 
established on this target for the infinTEM survey but an early spring prevented the 
survey completion. The 2010 Wabassi West VTEM survey extended this conductor 
towards the southwest. In 2011, Grid 1 was re-established and surveyed by Crone 
Geophysics.  Diamond drill hole 11WA-18 was drilled to further evaluate this target. 
 
Anomaly D was also a very subtle and ambiguous target and was interpreted as a 
possible "IP effect" from the VTEM signature.  It also coincides with a strongly magnetic 
layer. Surface sampling of the Wabassi Intrusion has suggested that this magnetic layer 
could represent the lowest levels of a rhythmic sequence and is therefore highly 
prospective for PGEs.  Hole 10WA-03 was drilled to test this anomaly and to assist in 
the geometry and understanding of the Wabassi Intrusion. 
 
Anomaly E was identified from the 2010 Wabassi West Survey and is of strong 
conductivity. A ground grid #3 was established in February 2011 and immediately 
surveyed by Crone Geophysics. Interpretation of this data by Condor Geophysics 
indicates that the conductor can be traced on all six lines of the ground grid. The 
parameters for three different models were developed by Condor Consulting.  The long 
section geometry of Anomaly E based on one of these models is provided in Figures 13 
& 14 and shows a doubly plunging body with the apex of the conductor located beneath 
line 400S.  Diamond drill holes 11WA-16, 17, 19 and 20 and, 12WA-25, 26, 27 and 28 
tested the anomaly. 
 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 47 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 

Figure 13: Long section geometry of Anomaly E with 2011 drillholes based on one of Condor's models. Drill-
hole pierce points are represented on the section.  NOTE: 11WA-17 and 11WA-20 were surveyed using the 
Earthprobe DCIP downhole method.  Results are discussed above and below. 

(Internal Northern Shield Resources Inc. 2012) 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 48 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 

Figure 14: Long section geometry of Anomaly E with 2011 and 2012 drill holes based on 
one of Condor's models.  Drill-hole pierce points are represented on the section.  White 
circles with black diamonds are pierce points from the 2012 drilling (12WA-25 through 
28). (Internal Northern Shield Resources Inc. 2012) 

 

9.3.2 2011 VTEM Survey 
 

The 2011 VTEM survey was not formally interpreted but the general review by Geotech 

(2011) indicates that: 

Block 2 contains 7 moderate to highly conductive targets, each with strong 
magnetic anomalies associated with them. The most conductive targets all lie 
along an east to west magnetic trend near the middle of the block. As well, there 

12WA-26 
12WA-25

12WA-27

12WA-28



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 49 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

are a number of targets with low conductance along magnetic anomalies (Figure 
15).  

2012 drilling tested targets from Block 2, Target Zones 2-4 and 2-9 (Figure 15).  
Target Zone 2-4 is represented by coincident magnetic and electromagnetic 
responses. It exhibits a conductivity of 899 siemens / meter and a conductivity 
thickness of 10,967 siemens.  It is a small target, modeled at 89 meters in strike 
and 12 meters in thickness, but extremely strong.  Drilling results are discussed 
in Section 10.  Target Zone 2-9 is also represented by coincident magnetic and 
electromagnetic responses.  It exhibits a conductivity of 83 siemens / meter and 
a conductivity thickness of 1,339 siemens.  It is a large target, modeled at 620 
meters in strike and 57 meters in thickness.  Drilling results are discussed in 
Section 10. 
 
Block 3 contains 7 targets ranging between moderate to highly conductive. Each 
of these targets lays along the same magnetic trend which arcs around a 
magnetic depression, at the south-western part of the block. Additionally, there 
are multiple low conductance targets along magnetic anomalies spread 
throughout the block (Figure 16).  

9.3.3 2012 Earthprobe Survey – Anomaly E – Drillholes 11WA-17 & 11WA-20 
 
At the request of Northern Shield Resources Inc. and Discovery Harbour Resources, 
Caracle Creek International Consulting Inc. (Caracle Creek) was commissioned to 
undertake an EarthProbe borehole resistivity and induced polarization (DCIP) survey. 
The objective of the survey was to determine the extent and orientation of mineralized 
intersections identified during drilling (to the extent possible) and determine if additional 
off-hole targets exist.  The geophysical survey was undertaken from February 6 – 12, 
2012 using the EarthProbe high resolution DCIP system.  The system can be 
configured for the collection of high resolution surface IP data, single borehole vertical 
profiles (VP), and/or multi-bore/surface-to-bore tomographic images. For this survey, 
data were collected using single borehole vertical profiling and borehole-to-borehole 
tomographic imaging.  The scope of work was to comprise VP and tomographic imaging 
of 4 boreholes (11WA-16, 11WA-17, 11WA-19 and 11WA-20).  11WA-16 and 11WA-19 
were blocked near surface and unable to be imaged.  
 
Results of the vertical profiling and borehole-to-borehole imaging from 11WA-17 and 
11WA-20 using the EarthProbe high resolution borehole DCIP system has shown: 
 

 Mineralized zones within exhibit a low resistivity (less than 300 Ohm.m); high 
chargeability is not definitively associated with the mineralized zones. 

 The narrow electrode separation of the EarthProbe system can detect 
mineralized regions as narrow as 3 m (narrower zones untested). 

 The mineralization intersected in 11WA-17 between 254.86 and 285.50 m 
extends at least 40 m off-hole. 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 50 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 Two zones of low resistivity and high chargeability were identified off-hole of 
11WA-17 at 100 – 140 m depth (35 m off-hole) and 160 – 190 m depth (40 m off-
hole); 

 One zone of low resistivity/high chargeability was detected off-hole of 11WA-20 
(180 – 280 m depth and approximately 60 m off-hole). 

 
Based on these limited results borehole DCIP, in particular resistivity appears to be a 
valuable tool for delineating the extent of Cu-Zn, Ag-Au mineralization at Anomaly E.  
With more data, 3D inversion of the vertical profiling and tomography data will enhance 
the spatial understanding of features of interest within the exploration area.

10.0 DIAMOND DRILLING  
 
In winter 2010, 13 diamond-drill holes for a total of 3,100 metres were completed on the 
Wabassi Property.  Ground and borehole InfiniTEM surveys were completed half way 
through the drill program and provided data for the targeting of the second half of the 
program.  The exploration program continued with a surface and borehole pulse EM 
surveys by Crone Geophysics and Exploration Ltd. in winter 2011 and was followed by 
7 diamond drill holes for a total of 2,150 metres.  Hole locations are illustrated on Figure 
12. 
 
 
10.2 Drill Hole Description 
 

10WA-01 
Collar UTMN 5,728,914 EOH 237 metres
Collar UTME 527,659 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 120° Main Lithology 
fine-medium grained Mela 

Gabbronorite, Peridotite

Dip at Collar -65° Main Mineralization Patches of fine cpy, po, pnt

 
 
Drill-hole 10WA-01 was drilled to test Anomaly C on Line 4470 that was subsequently 
found to continue another 1,000 meters to the southwest after the completion of the 
2010 Wabassi West Survey. 
 
The drill-hole encountered fine to medium grained greenish-grey melagabbro from 13 m 
to 205 m, interspersed with a multi-phased dioritic dyke.  The gabbro transitions into 
peridotite within the last 30 metres.  Interfaces between cyclic layering can be observed 
within the gabbro. 
 
No significant mineralization was intersected though small patches of disseminated and 
primary textured chalcopyrite, pyrrhotite and pentlandite were observed near the top of 
the peridotite.  The mineralization occurs near and at the contact of gabbroic material 
with the peridotite, suggesting either magma mixing or slumping of semi-solidified 
magma into the underlying magma. 
 
The source of the VTEM anomaly was not explained by this drill-hole. 
 

10WA-02 
Collar UTMN 5,734,539 EOH 152 metres
Collar UTME 531,967 Dip of Layering Unknown

Drilling Azimuth 165° Main Lithology Gabbro, Granodiorite

Dip at Collar -75° Main Mineralization Semi-massive py in siliceous zone 

 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 56 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

Drill-hole 10WA-02 was drilled to test a moderate, single line EM anomaly (Anomaly B) 
on Line 4020 on the east side of the intrusion. Gabbroic rocks were intersected at the 
top of the hole but reverted to various phases of granodiorite below 62 m.  Potassic 
alteration was commonly seen throughout the gabbro.  A silicified and pyrite-rich zone 
with up to 25% pyrite was intersected from 105 m to 122 m.  In the lower portion of the 
interval, the pyrite is controlled by fractures at 40° to core angle. The interval contains 
weakly elevated silver (1 ppm Ag).  All gold values were low except two intercepts of 0.1 
and 0.2 ppm gold. 
 

10WA-03 
Collar UTMN 5,734,265 EOH 267 metres
Collar UTME 527,705 Dip of Layering 0° 

Drilling Azimuth 325° Main Lithologies 

medium grained Leuco 
Gabbronorite, minor pegmatoidal 

Melagabbro and fine grained 
Gabbronorite and Olivine Gabbro

Dip at Collar -50° Main Mineralization 

 
Drill-hole 10WA-03 was not targeting a VTEM anomaly as such though a weak 
conductor is present along this horizon on line 4260 (Anomaly D).  This hole is located 
along the longest and thickest portion of the magnetic layers that marks a transition 
between two distinct parts of the intrusion. No outcrop has been observed along this 
trend and the DEM profiles from the VTEM survey show a distinct trough corresponding 
to this magnetic layer.  The B-field plots show that the surficial sediments filling the 
trough are relatively conductive.  This all suggests that the underlying layer could be 
partially serpentinized ultramafic rock.  If this was the case it could represent a fresh 
pulse of primitive magma into the chamber acting as an ideal catalyst for the formation 
of low sulphidization reef-style PGE mineralization. 
 
No sulphides were intersected in the hole.  The core, as logged in the field, was 
described as a series of gabbronorites, olivine-gabbronorites and minor intervals of very 
coarse-grained pyroxenites, with all lithologies containing magnetite. 
 
Preliminary review of the geochemistry and thin sections combined with the drill logs 
indicates the upper portion of the hole (0-170 m) to be dominantly composed of 
medium-grained leucogabbro, leucogabbronorites and olivine-gabbronorites.  The mafic 
minerals in this interval are generally all interstitial in nature, highly altered, and the 
olivine grains display a distinct reaction rim.  Both primary and secondary magnetite is 
present.  At 53.0 to 53.3 metres, a very conspicuous pegmatoidal melagabbro (norite) 
was intersected.  It contains pyroxene and magnetite crystals up to 4 cm in diameter.  
Several smaller intervals of the same rock type were intersected in the upper portion of 
this hole.  The contacts of these intervals are generally at a high angle to the core axis 
and hence these may be discordant, devolatilization pipes within the intrusion. 
 
At 171.4 metres, a 9 metre thick peridotite horizon marks the transition to another 
distinct unit.  This unit is generally finer grained and the mafic minerals are pristine and 
lack the reaction rims seen in the unit above.  Lithologies include gabbronorites and 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 57 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

olivine-gabbros (near troctolite composition).  The olivine is remarkably fresh and is 
generally much more abundant than pyroxenes. 
 
The hole was relatively lightly sampled but the geochemistry shows a distinct transition 
between samples collected at 158 m and 219 m.  Both units are strongly fractionated, 
as indicated by very low Cr/V ratios, but the up-hole unit is highly evolved with 
phosphorus in the 2,000-3,000 ppm range.  The down-hole unit contains a greater mafic 
(and Mg) component than the up-hole unit, though the Ni and Cr content are remarkably 
low, with both elements assaying at less than 10 ppm. 
 

10WA-04 
Collar UTMN 5,733,240 EOH 302 metres
Collar UTME 527,659 Dip of Layering 30° to core axis, locally

Drilling Azimuth 145° Main Lithologies 
medium grained Norite, 

Gabbronorites and Troctolite

Dip at Collar -75° Main Mineralization 
Fine disseminated to net-textured 

Cpy, Po, Pnt
 
A variety of mafic cumulate rocks were intersected in hole 10WA-04.  This hole was 
targeting a portion of anomaly A1.  Although actual layering was not clearly identified, 
the composition varied from top to bottom with leuconorite and gabbronorite at the top, 
norite and gabbronorite in the middle and troctolite near the bottom.  
 
Finely disseminated and net-textured sulphides (chalcopyrite, pyrrhotite and 
pentlandite) were observed locally and seem to correspond to a small but noticeable Ni 
enrichment.  Very limited geochemistry and assaying was completed in this hole but 
both seem to correlate with the petrographic observations.  The indications are that 
progressively more primitive layers were intersected in the down hole direction (i.e., the 
intrusion is right way up at that location). 
 
The source of the anomaly was not explained in this hole. 
 

10WA-05 
Collar UTMN 5,733,240 EOH 342 metres
Collar UTME 527,659 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 325° Main Lithologies 
Norite, Olivine-norite, Gabbro, 

Harzburgite

Dip at Collar -75° Main Mineralization Massive and semi-massive Po, 
Py, Cpy

 
 
This hole was drilled to test the A1 anomaly on line 4400 and intersected alternating 
mafic and ultramafic cumulate-textured rocks.  The mafic lithologies are mostly norites, 
olivine-norites and hornblende-gabbros.  Some of the hornblende appears primary, at 
least locally, where it forms pristine-looking oikocrysts, however, it is more common to 
find hornblende clearly replacing the pyroxenes (alteration/metamorphism) where 
remnants of the pyroxenes are still visible.  The ultramafic intersections are peridotitic, 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 58 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

mostly harzburgites (orthopyroxene oikocrysts are typically much more abundant than 
clinopyroxene) but also lhertzolites (with large clinopyroxene oikocrysts) and olivine-
orthopyroxenites (more abundant orthopyroxene than olivine). 
 
Two large zones of massive to semi-massive and net textured sulphides of about 45 
metres each starting at 116 m and at 252 m, were intersected and explained the 
anomaly.  The two mineralized intersections are located at the interface between mafic 
and ultramafic rocks but above the ultramafic rocks for the shallower intersection and 
below for the deeper one.  Initial observations suggest that there may be repetition of 
layers due to folding or displacement along faults, and that the stratigraphy, at least in 
the upper portion of the hole, is right-way-up. 
 
The actual host of the sulphide intersection is difficult to determine because all silicates 
observed in thin sections have been transformed to chlorite, tremolite (or other colorless 
amphibole?) and minor talc (or other white mica), serpentine and probably clay 
minerals. 
 
The composition of the sulphides is mainly pyrrhotite and pyrite with subordinate 
chalcopyrite. The sulphides may occur interstitially (net-texture) but also form veins and 
even breccias locally.  Assay results surprisingly did not return significant PGEs or 
nickel. 
 

10WA-06 
Collar UTMN 5,733,145 EOH 216 metres
Collar UTME 525,735 Dip of Layering Unknown

Drilling Azimuth 145° Main Lithology 
Fine-Medium Grained 

Gabbronorite

Dip at Collar -65° Main Mineralization Net-textured Cpy
 
Hole 10WA-06 intersected only mafic lithologies, most gabbronorite and gabbro. No 
whole-rock samples were taken and therefore no thin sections were made to identify the 
rock types more accurately. 
 
Two small zones of disseminated to net-textured sulphides, mostly chalcopyrite, were 
intersected around 85 m and 105 m explaining the A1 anomaly at this location.  These 
zones were sampled and returned copper values up to 1.2% over 1.04 metres.  This 
interval was contained within a 4.4 meter core interval averaging 0.67% copper.  One 
very noticeable geochemical feature in this hole is the abnormally low nickel content.  
This, along with low chrome and high phosphorus may indicate that the rocks analysed 
represent a section located fairly high up in the stratigraphy of the intrusion. 
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 59 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

10WA-07 

Collar UTMN 5,732,415 EOH 213 metres
Collar UTME 525,355 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 145° Main Lithology Pg-porphyritic Volcanics, Gabbro

Dip at Collar -85° Main Mineralization Po, Py, Sph, Cpy, Ag

 
This hole targeting anomaly A2; intersected significant VMS-style zinc, silver and 
copper mineralisation.  The top portion of the hole intersected a volcanic assemblage 
composed mostly of plagioclase-porphyritic massive flows.  It is also possible that parts 
of it are synvolcanic dikes.  The general composition of the assemblage is dacitic to 
rhyolitic.  The 0.5-2 mm plagioclase phenocrysts (10 to 15%) of the rock lie in a 
crystallized matrix of fine plagioclase, quartz, hornblende and biotite with minor chloritic, 
epidote and carbonate alterations. 
 
The mineralized intersection consists of a 50 metre zone of massive to semi-massive 
sulphides between the depths of 40 and 90 metres approximately. The sulphides are 
mainly pyrrhotite, pyrite and sphalerite in varying proportions, with minor chalcopyrite.  
The sulphides seem to exhibit replacement textures.  The contact zone below the 
sulphides also contains significant amount of veins and fragments.  Assay results 
display very high zinc and silver content throughout the sulphide intersection.  Silver 
content is related to elevated lead and generally, the highest silver is associated with 
low zinc content. 
 
The contact with the gabbroic units that forms the bottom part of this hole consists of a 
broad zone of volcanic rocks injected with gabbro dikes from 100 m to 150 m.  From 
150m to the end of the hole gabbro is present.  
 

10WA-08 
Collar UTMN 5,733,062 EOH 307 metres
Collar UTME 525,979 Dip of Layering Unknown

Drilling Azimuth 290° Main Lithology 
Gabbronorite, Norite, Troctolite, 

Harzburgite

Dip at Collar -55° Main Mineralization NA
 
This hole was designed to test an InfinTEM target modelled by Abitibi Geophysics at the 
A1 anomaly.  No mineralization was intersected, though the modelled position and 
orientation of this target was subsequently refined.  The first 90 metres of drill-hole 
10WA-08 was initially logged as volcanic rocks but was subsequently re-logged as 
olivine-poor gabbros and gabbronorites.  The rocks are injected with numerous granitic 
and diabase dikes along with quartz-carbonate and other veins, resulting in strong 
alteration.  From 90 metres down, a sequence of gabbronorite, norite, troctolite, and 
harzburgite are present.  In thin sections, the units observed are very fresh and primary 
textures are very well preserved.  It appears that olivine-bearing units become more 
abundant towards the bottom of this hole, which may indicate that the stratigraphy of the 
intrusion is intersected from higher to lower sequences.
