10WA-09 
Collar UTMN 5,733,142 EOH 192 metres
Collar UTME 525,762 Dip of Layering Unknown

Drilling Azimuth 290° Main Lithology Gabbronorite, Norite, Peridotite

Dip at Collar -60° Main Mineralization Po, Py, Cpy

 
This hole intersected two zones enriched in sulphides at 25-80 m and 145-160 m, 
mostly composed of pyrrhotite and pyrite that would explain the A1 anomaly targeted.  A 
few short sections enriched in chalcopyrite were also intersected and the entire hole 
displays unusually low values in nickel.  The most sulphide-rich samples also contain 
anomalous zinc in the order of 0.5%.  Two sulphide-rich thin sections were studied. The 
host rock is difficult to assess because it is completely altered to chlorite with white mica 
(talc or sericite?) and dark clay minerals.  Some possible remnants of orthopyroxene 
were observed, which may indicate that the host rock was a gabbronorite or norite. 
 
Between the mineralized sections, rocks are described as gabbronorite, norite and 
peridotite but because this hole intersected rocks that are very altered and foliated, only 
remnants of textures are found locally.  Ultramafic rocks described as peridotites but 
very altered; occurs over a 15 m core length commencing at 54 m.   
 

10WA-10a 
Collar UTMN 5,733,129 EOH 171 metres
Collar UTME 525,800 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 070° Main Lithology 
Gabbronorite, Olivine-Norite, 

Harzburgite

Dip at Collar -60° Main Mineralization Po, Py, Cpy

 
Hole 10WA-10 was designed to target the A1 anomaly.  Hole 10WA-10 was first 
abandoned around 30 metres because the drill was not able to get through the thick 
layer of loose unconsolidated overburden at an angle of 60°. 
 
The drill was repositioned and hole 10WA-10a commenced.  The hole intersected a 7 
metre zone at 130 m of massive to semi-massive sulphides composed mainly of 
pyrrhotite and pyrite with some chalcopyrite around 130 m.  A few short sections with 
disseminated chalcopyrite were also intersected.  As in drill-hole 10WA-09, the 
sulphide-rich section are anomalous  in zinc and copper but in this hole, nickel content 
is higher, partly representing normal olivine content but probably also the presence of 
minor pentlandite or nickeliferous pyrrhotite.  
 
The drill-hole intersected a well-layered sequence of mafic-ultramafic lithologies with 
coarse-grained gabbronorites, olivine gabbronorites and harzburgites interlayered with 
fine to medium grained olivine leuconorites and melanorites.  The rocks are generally 
fresh and the primary textures and mineralogy are very well preserved. The ultramafic 
component of both the fine grained sequence and the coarse grained sequence 
increases down-hole suggesting the stratigraphy is right way up. 
 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 61 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

It is interesting to note that the thin section made from core at 132 m displays semi-
massive sulphide (~30%) along with very fresh silicate mineralogy with well-preserved 
plagioclase cumulates and ortho and clinopyroxenes, partly transformed to hornblende 
and biotite but still recognisable.  In all previous sections observed to date for this 
program which contained more than 15% sulphides, all silicates are altered to a mixture 
of mostly chlorite and amphiboles and primary textures are obliterated.  This sample 
clearly demonstrates that magmatic sulphides are precipitating within the intrusion and 
that the massive sulphide intersections that are found in the intrusion are not large rafts 
of the VMS-type sulphides of the host volcanic rocks.  Olivine-bearing rocks with clear 
net textured sulphides were also found earlier in mineralized intersections which are 
interpreted as precipitation of sulphides within the intrusion. 
 

10WA-11 
Collar UTMN 5,733,287 EOH 288 metres
Collar UTME 525,948 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 250° Main Lithology Gabbronorite, Norite

Dip at Collar -68° Main Mineralization Cpy

 
Gabbronorite and norite dominate this hole with possible olivine-bearing units near the 
bottom.  These rocks are more altered than typical in the Wabassi Intrusion, most likely 
because they are cut by several diabase and granitoid dikes that are typically 
accompanied by quartz-carbonate veins.  Several shear zones a few meters in width 
were also intersected in this hole. 
 
Possible layering defined by 1 cm rings with different concentrations of plagioclase 
versus pyroxene cumulates was observed at 29 m depth and is almost perfectly 
perpendicular to core axis. 
 
This hole did not intersect massive sulphides but intersected several zones with 2-3% 
disseminated chalcopyrite and patches of net textured pyrrhotite.  It is not definite that 
the A1 anomaly was intersected.

Gabbronorite and olivine-gabbronorite are the dominant lithologies in this hole.

gabbronorite. 
 
This hole intersected massive sulphides composed of pyrrhotite, pyrite and chalcopyrite

to 5% chalcopyrite are also found below the mineralized section.  Gabbronorites and

olivine-gabbronorites are found above and below the massive sulphide intersection and

10WA-13 
Collar UTMN 5,732,994 EOH 264 metres
Collar UTME 525,409 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 290° Main Lithology 
Pg-porphyritic Volcanics, 

Gabbro, Gabbronorite

Dip at Collar -50° Main Mineralization Po, Py, Sph, Cpy, Ag
 
This drill-hole was designed to intersect the widest portion of the A2 conductor, as 
modeled from the InfiniTEM survey.  From top to bottom, drill-hole 10WA-13 intersected 
andesitic rocks interpreted as lava flows, felsic volcanics dominated by quartz-phyric 
porphyry with lesser amounts of feldspar porphyry, aphanitic rhyolite and finally a 
gabbroic unit followed by a gabbronorite unit. 
 
There are three main mineralized intervals associated to the felsic volcanics.  The first 
one is observed from 42.4 to 48.3 metres.  It is capped by the andesite and consists of 
5 to 50% pyrite, trace to 30% pyrrhotite, 5 to locally 30% magnetite, traces of 
chalcopyrite and also contains trace to 5% sphalerite in the lower meter of the unit. In 
the top half of this unit, the sulphides form the matrix of a breccia with clasts of quartz 
porphyry with possible chloritoid.  In the lower half, the sulphides are better described 
as impregnations within a fine-grained chloritized felsic to intermediate volcanic rock. 
The second mineralized interval is between 53.4 and 60.8 metres, capped by a feldspar 
porphyry.  The top half consists of trace to 10% pyrite, trace to locally 10% pyrrhotite, 
trace to 10% sphalerite and trace to 1% chalcopyrite, disseminated and as veinlets 
within an aphanitic rhyolite that shows signs of chlorite, biotite and possible cordierite 
secondary development.  The bottom half consists of a quartz-porphyry that is cherty 
and banded locally and contains traces to 7% disseminated chalcopyrite.  The third 
mineralized interval is between 64.2 and 82.3 metres and comprises a 10 metre-thick 
top portion of quartz porphyry hosting trace to 5% pyrite, trace to 5% pyrrhotite, trace to 
5% sphalerite and trace to 5% chalcopyrite as veinlets and disseminations.  The bottom 
portion is composed of an 8 metre section of massive sulphides, mostly pyrite and/or 
pyrrhotite with traces of chalcopyrite and sphalerite; locally there are minor sections with 
up to 10% chalcopyrite. 
 
Immediately underneath the massive sulphides, the contact with the underlying gabbro 
consists of a hybrid zone, possibly a breccia, composed of a chaotic mixture of gabbro, 
felsic volcanics and granodioritic rocks.  This unit contains trace to 10% pyrrhotite, trace 
to 3% pyrite, trace to 1% chalcopyrite and trace of sphalerite.  A unit of massive gabbro 
underlies the hybrid zone and contains local traces of pyrrhotite and scarce traces of 
pyrite and chalcopyrite.  Two sub-rounded zoned "bubbles" or clasts of semi-massive 
sulphides with concentrations of chalcopyrite on one side and pyrrhotite on the opposite 
side are reminiscent of textures observed in other Ni-Cu magmatic systems.  The 
bottom unit consists of a spotty (orthopyroxene clots or phenocrysts) or "leopard-
textured" gabbronorite with suggestions of magmatic layering indicated by variable 
proportions of plagioclase and orthopyroxene. Both the gabbro and the gabbronorite are 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 63 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

cut by feldspar porphyry dikes very similar to the volcanic unit observed near the top of 
the hole. 
 

11WA-14 
Collar UTMN 5,733,051 EOH 473 metres
Collar UTME 525,715 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 107° Main Lithology 
Gabbronorite, Diorite, Gabbro, 

Norite, Mafic Volcanic

Dip at Collar -58° Main Mineralization Semi-massive, Po, Py, Cpy

 
Hole 11WA-14 was drilled to test a large but deep conductor modelled by Condor 
Consulting at the A1 anomaly.  This drill hole intersected mainly a large section of 
gabbronorite from top to bottom with smaller units of gabbro, norite, diorite and a mafic 
volcanic rock.  Gabbronorite and gabbro are the dominant lithologies present in this 
hole.  Clinopyroxene and orthopyroxene oikocrysts and cumulate textures can be 
observed in some gabbronorite sections where the rock is not strongly silicified.  Diorite, 
norite and mafic volcanic units represent smaller (2-10 m) stratigraphic units 
interlayered within the gabbronorite and gabbro units.  Rock magnetism and grain size 
vary from not magnetic to magnetic and fine to coarse-grained respectively in 
gabbronorite, diorite, gabbro, and norite.  The mafic volcanic unit occurs as 3-11 metre 
intervals. 
 
Silica alteration occurs throughout the hole and ranges from moderate to intense 
making rock and mineral identification difficult.  Other alteration phases are sericite, 
chlorite, carbonate, biotite, and epidote. Alteration is so intense in some sections that 
the protolith is unknown.  These sections of core are logged as "alteration zone" but are 
suspected to be a gabbro. 
 
There is one zone containing semi-massive sulphides of approximately one meter 
sampled from 443 m to 444 m.  Trace to 20% sulphides occur from approximately 435-
455 m and are hosted by a breccia unit.  Fragments of disseminated sulphides (pyrite, 
pyrrhotite, and chalcopyrite) are present throughout the hole.  Minor sphalerite was 
observed at the top of the hole. 
 
Assay results indicate no significant zones of mineralization but there are a few 
interesting samples worth noting.  Diorite contains the highest Cu (1.5% over 0.96 
meters) and Ag (29.3 ppm) values in the hole at a depth of 80 metres; this is contained 
within a 2.76 meter interval averaging 1.32 % copper.  Gabbronorite samples from 201-
210, 284, 306-308, 326-327, 332-353, 360-366, and 385-391 m contain the highest Cr 
(50-2000 ppm) and Ni (70-700 ppm) values in this hole. 
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 64 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

11WA-15 
Collar UTMN 5,733,968 EOH 194 metres
Collar UTME 525,551 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 90° Main Lithology Gabbronorite, Gabbro, Mafic Flow

Dip at Collar -50° Main Mineralization Disseminated Po, Py, Cpy, Sph

 
Hole 11WA-15 was drilled to test a highly conductive, near surface target as modelled 
by Condor Consulting on the A1 anomaly area.  This hole intersected three main 
lithologies including a gabbro, gabbronorite and mafic volcanic rocks.  The upper 
section of the hole from 20-59 m is composed of interlayered volcanic rocks and 
gabbro. The mafic volcanic rocks are generally aphanitic to fine-grained. The gabbro is 
coarser grained (medium to coarse grained).  Interlayered gabbronorite and gabbro 
units make up most of the hole from 59 to 170 m.  The last 24 meters from 170 to 194 is 
mainly a gabbronorite with 1-3 m mafic dikes. 
 
A zone of minor sulphide mineralization was intersected at the top of the hole from 29 to 
59 m and is hosted in mixed mafic volcanic rocks and gabbro.  The composition of the 
sulphides is mainly pyrrhotite, pyrite, chalcopyrite, and sphalerite.  The sulphides occur 
as stringers, blebs and disseminations and are fine to medium grained.  Sulphide 
abundance varies from mostly trace to 5% but can be up to 20% over smaller 
intercepts.  Copper values in the mineralized zone are significant and vary from 1,000 to 
15,000 ppm.  High copper values correspond to elevated S, Ag and Au values.  Zinc 
content is very low (averaging 150 ppm).  The copper mineralization is proximal to the 
modelled depth of the InifiTEM target but the amount of sulphides seen is not sufficient 
to create an EM response and hence can't be the cause of the anomaly itself.  
However, the mineralization seen in drill-core may be a halo of disseminated 
mineralization surrounding massive sulphides. 
   
All lithologies are low in Cr and Ni with average values of <10 ppm Cr and <20 ppm Ni. 
The gabbronorite is relatively high in Al, Fe, and V and low in Cr, Cu, Ni, and Zn. 
 

11WA-16 
Collar UTMN 5,728,075 EOH 222 metres
Collar UTME 524,924 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 320° Main Lithology 
Mafic Flow, Rhyolite, Ultramafic 

Volcanic

Dip at Collar -60° Main Mineralization 
Massive to Semi-massive Po, Py, 

Cpy, Sph
 
Drill-hole 11WA-16 was drilled to test Anomaly E where the conductor is modelled as 
being nearest to surface. 
 
This hole intersected three main lithologies including possibly ultramafic volcanic rocks, 
mafic metavolcanic rocks of andesitic composition and felsic metavolcanic rocks with or 
without blue quartz eyes.  The top 60 meters of the hole from 27 to 87 m intersected a 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 65 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

black rock with amphibole phenocrysts and olivine. This unit is currently interpreted to 
be ultramafic volcanic based on geochemical data of rock samples containing between 
18% and 25% MgO.  Thin sections were also made of this unit but the rock is highly 
altered and it is difficult to confirm that it is in fact a volcanic package.  However, 
vesicle-like features were observed in the core and the absences of the usual textures 
that are perfectly preserved in the ultramafic intrusive rocks in the area seem to point to 
a volcanic origin.  The next 73 meters intersected a mafic volcanic assemblage 
composed of massive flows and breccia.  These rocks contain fractures and quartz 
veins with minor chalcopyrite, pyrrhotite and pyrite.  
 
A 40 meter mineralized zone from 160-200 m contains sections of disseminated, 
brecciated, semi-massive and massive sulphides varying from 5-90%.  The composition 
of the sulphides is mainly pyrrhotite, pyrite, sphalerite, and chalcopyrite.  The sulphides 
occur in veins, between fragments and as disseminations.  Sphalerite occurrence is 
very high with Zn values up to 15% in some 1 metre sections.  Chalcopyrite is also 
significant with copper concentrations up to 4% in 1 metre sections.  Gold and silver 
assay values are up to 825 ppb and 194 ppm respectively (1 metre sections).  Chlorite 
and biotite with minor white mica are the most common alterations present associated 
with mineralization.  The host of the mineralization is a chlorite altered blue-quartz 
rhyolite. 
 
The last 22 meters of the hole intersected a massive rhyolite containing distinct blue 
quartz eyes, and is variably altered by chlorite, silica, biotite, and sericite.  Veins and 
veinlets of quartz and carbonate are common.  The bottom contact of the mineralisation 
is sharp and no sulphides are present within the massive rhyolite. 
 

11WA-17 
Collar UTMN 5,728,075 EOH 326 metres
Collar UTME 528,290 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 135° Main Lithology 
Granite, Mafic Flow, Rhyolite, 

Mafic Dike

Dip at Collar -56° Main Mineralization 
Massive and Semi-massive Po, 

Py, Cpy, Sph
 
Drill-hole 11WA-17 was drilled to test Anomaly E along strike (~100 metres) from 
11WA-16.  The top 79 meters intersected a medium to coarse grained granite with 
minor to strong sericite, silica, epidote and potassic alteration.  Granitic pegmatite veins 
cross cut the entire granite section.  The granite also varies from moderately magnetic 
to very weakly magnetic.  A smaller (11 m) granite intrusion occurs from 124-135 m.  A 
felsic volcanic unit is intersected from 91 to 142 m.  It is commonly very altered and 
silicified with almost complete loss of texture.  Minor disseminated pyrite and 
chalcopyrite in veins are present in places.  Interlayered massive intermediate to felsic 
flows and breccias are intersected throughout the remainder of the hole.  The rhyolite 
contains distinct blue quartz eyes, can be massive or brecciated, and is commonly 
silica, chlorite and biotite altered.  Minor disseminated sulphides occur in both massive 
and blue-quartz porphyritic rhyolite units and consist of trace to 20% pyrrhotite, pyrite 
and chalcopyrite 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 66 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

Variable mineralization occurs from 260 to 285 m with three main mineralized zones.  
The first mineralized zone is approximately 4 meters of disseminated to semi-massive 
sulphides (259-263 m) including pyrrhotite, pyrite and chalcopyrite, which are interstitial 
between fragments and as veins.  The second mineralized zone is a 3 meter layer of 
massive sulphides from 273-276 m.  The proportion of each sulphide varies but 
generally the order of abundance is sphalerite, chalcopyrite, pyrite and pyrrhotite 
making up 90% of the rock.  The sulphides occur interstitially, as veins, breccias locally, 
possibly banded, and disseminations.  The third mineralized zone is also a 3 meters 
core interval (true thickness unknown) from 282-285 m.  The first 1.5 m consists of fine 
to coarse grained massive sulphides (75%) such as sphalerite and pyrite with moderate 
pyrrhotite and chalcopyrite.  Sulphide abundance decreases over the next meter to 50% 
sulphides containing mostly pyrrhotite and chalcopyrite with moderate pyrite and minor 
sphalerite.  Felsic volcanic rock and mafic dikes occur throughout, before and after 
mineralization and partition the mineralized zones. Various breccias and massive blue-
quartz eye bearing felsic units are the host to sulphide mineralization and contain trace 
to 20% sulphides.  Zinc values reach as high as 25% (272.9 to 273.6m for 0.7 meters @ 
25.3% Zn) followed by copper values up to 9% (273.6 to 274.2m for 0.6 meters @ 
9.90% Cu.  These are contained within a 3.6 meter core interval from 272.4 to 276 
meters averaging 5.81% copper and 9.73% zinc).  The highest Au and Ag values are 
1390 ppb Au and 217 ppm Ag in assay samples collected from this same zone, each 
over 0.7 and 0.6 m respectively.  True thickness of the 3 – 6 meter core interval of 
higher grade zinc and copper is unknown. 
 

11WA-18 
Collar UTMN 5,728,932 EOH 128 metres
Collar UTME 527,838 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 320° Main Lithology Gabbro, Granite, Gabbronorite 

Dip at Collar -60° Main Mineralization Disseminated Po, Py, Cpy

 
Drill-hole 11WA-18 was drilled to test the strongest portion of Anomaly C as defined by 
the Crone pulse EM survey.  The top portion of the hole intersected a gabbro 
interlayered with granite from 14 to 80 m.  Both gabbro and granite rocks range from 
coarse to pegmatitic in grain size.  The last 30 meters intersected alternating and 
normally graded fine and coarse grained gabbros.  The upper portion of the hole is 
mostly pegmatitic and therefore overall coarser than the bottom of the hole.  The 
pegmatic gabbro and gabbronorite contain significant amounts of magnetite, over 10%.  
Alteration minerals include quartz, chlorite, carbonate, and biotite as veins and within 
the matrix.   
 
No significant sulphide mineralization was intersected in this hole that would explain the 
anomaly.  Minor disseminated sulphides are present including chalcopyrite, pyrrhotite 
and pyrite. Mineralization is generally <10% sulphides with some locally large pyrrhotite 
fragments. 
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 67 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

11WA-19 
Collar UTMN 5,728,031 EOH 362 metres
Collar UTME 524,967 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 315° Main Lithology 
Quartz-Feldspar Porphyry, 

Ultramafic Volcanic, Felsic Flows 
and Breccia, Mafic Flows

Dip at Collar -60° Main Mineralization Semi-massive Py, Po, Cpy

 
Drill-hole 11WA-19 was positioned to test the continuation of the mineralization 
intersected in 11WA-16 at anomaly E.  This hole intersected various lithologies 
including felsic to ultramafic volcanic rocks and felsic to intermediate plutonic rocks.  
The top portion of the hole from 28-52 m intersected mafic volcanic flows and breccias 
with quartz-feldspar porphyry and mafic dikes.  The volcanic rocks are intermediate to 
mafic, green, and not magnetic to very magnetic and altered by chlorite, sericite, and 
silica.  Ultramafic volcanic rocks were intersected from 52-130 m.  This section of core 
was poorly drilled and appears striated therefore textures are difficult to see. The next 
28 meters (211-239 m) contain intermixed breccia, and massive flows. These units are 
usually strongly biotite; chlorite and silica altered making it difficult to distinguish 
textures and mineralogy. 
 
A small 30 cm massive sulphide zone was intersected at 232.7 m and is composed 
mostly of pyrrhotite and pyrite with minor chalcopyrite.  Below the mineralized zone is a 
5 meter section of minor (1-30%) disseminated sulphides.  The host is difficult to 
determine because the rock is very strongly altered.  Zinc, copper and silver values are 
very low (<371 ppm Zn, <3530 ppm Cu and <4 ppm Ag) in the mineralized zone.   
 
The bottom portion of the hole from 239-343 m, below the mineralized zone, is 
comprised of alternating rhyolite and felsic breccia units.  The rhyolite is distinguished 
by the presence of blue quartz eyes and its massive, siliceous texture.  The felsic 
breccia contains large fragments and no quartz eyes.  Both rocks contain trace to 15% 
disseminated sulphides and variable chlorite, biotite and silica alteration.  The blue 
quartz bearing rhyolite hosts the highest Zn values intersected in this hole from 240-246 
m, which range between 0.33-0.88% Zn.  Copper values are low (<0.23%). 
 
This hole ended in 19 meters of massive, medium-grained diorite with quartz, 
carbonate, epidote and chlorite veins. 
 

11WA-20 
Collar UTMN  EOH 443 metres
Collar UTME  Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth  Main Lithologies 
Granite, Rhyolite, and Felsic 

Breccia

Dip at Collar  Main Mineralization

Hole 11WA-20 was drilled to delineate the extent of the massive sulphide zone found in 
drill-holes 11WA-16 and 17 and to test anomaly E at deeper levels.  The drill-hole 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 68 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

deflected to the right with the result that the hole hit the very edge of the modelled 
conductor, not the center as targeted. 
 
The drill-hole intersected a large section of granite from 16 m to 287 m. The granite 
shows variable intensity of sericite, potassic, chlorite, epidote, and silica alteration and 
contains several mafic fragments from 0.5-15 cm.  Several mafic bands and quartz-
chlorite veins are oriented at 15-30° to core axis. Below the granite unit is a 121 m 
section of rhyolite from 287 m to 408 m interspaced with diorite and massive flows.  This 
rhyolite unit is locally strongly to moderately altered by chlorite, biotite, silica, and 
carbonate minerals, and is distinguished by the characteristic presence of blue quartz 
eyes.  It contained none to 1% disseminated pyrite, chalcopyrite and pyrrhotite.  
Rhyolite assay samples from 364.5-367.5 m have copper values ranging from 0.4-1.0%, 
30-80 ppm silver, 60-134 ppb gold and very low zinc (500-750 ppm).  Several 1-2 m 
sections of diorite dikes composed of mainly quartz and plagioclase and oriented at 15-
20° to core axis cut the rhyolite.  Some portions of the rhyolite are also aphanitic and do 
not display the blue quartz eyes. 
 
The zone of massive to semi-massive sulphides was intersected between 408 m and 
411 m cross cut by a 20 cm rhyolite dike? at 410 m.  The host of the sulphide 
intersection is a rhyolite that varies in texture from massive at the top to brecciated at 
the bottom of the mineralized intersection.  The composition of the sulphides is mainly 
pyrrhotite, sphalerite, pyrite and chalcopyrite.  The sulphides occur as massive to semi-
massive lenses, stringers and disseminations.  The mineralized zone contains very high 
zinc values (2-10% Zn over 1 metre intervals) but only elevated gold silver and copper.  
 
A mafic variolitic volcanic sequence was intersected below the rhyolite-hosted 
mineralization.  This unit is aphanitic, contains variable chlorite, carbonate, biotite, and 
silica alteration and <1% disseminated pyrite.   
 

12WA-21 – Anomaly 2-9 
Collar UTMN 5,718,430 EOH 155 metres

Hole 12WA-21 was drilled to test a moderate to strong conductivity anomaly possessing 
a coincident magnetic signature from Target Zone 2-9.  9.2 meters of overburden were 
encountered before entering mafic volcanic rocks (quartz-chlorite-biotite schists).  Felsic 
volcanic rocks (quartz-phyric sericite schists) began at 37 meters and dominated the 
lithologic units encountered for the remainder of the hole, with intermittent gabbro 
intrusives present and randomly spaced.  Massive and semi-massive sulfides, 
dominated by pyrrhotite and lesser pyrite were encountered from 63.9 to 89.8 meters 
(25.9 meters), followed by 3.7 meters of stringer sulfide mineralization with traces of 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 69 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

chalcopyrite in veins and fractures, hosted in altered felsic protolith.  This stringer zone 
appears footwall to the main sulfide interval. Present interpretation suggests this hole 
intercepted a distal facies of mineralization to a main VMS vent system at a 
stratigraphically equivalent position in the volcanic section. 
 

12WA-22 – Anomaly 2-9 
Collar UTMN 5,718,019 EOH 182 metres
Collar UTME 510,308 Dip of Layering Uncertain

Bimodal volcanic, felsic-dominant

from 130.5 to 137.8m
 

Hole 12WA-22 was drilled to test a moderate to strong conductivity anomaly possessing 
a coincident magnetic signature from Target Zone 2-9. 23 meters of overburden were 
encountered before entering mafic volcanic rocks (quartz-garnet-biotite schists).  Felsic 
volcanic rocks and felsic breccias (quartz-phyric sericite schists) began at 133 meters 
and dominated the lithologic units encountered for the remainder of the hole.  Massive 
and semi-massive sulfides, dominated by pyrrhotite and lesser pyrite were encountered 
from 130.5 to 137.8 meters (7.3 meters).  Present interpretation suggests this hole 
intercepted a distal facies of mineralization to a main VMS vent system at a 
stratigraphically equivalent position in the volcanic section. 
 

12WA-23 – Anomaly 2-4 
Collar UTMN 5,719,079 EOH 52 metres
Collar UTME 513,276 Dip of Layering Uncertain 

Drilling Azimuth 0° Main Lithology 
Intermediate volcanic-flow & 

breccia

Dip at Collar -55° Main Mineralization 28.6-30.2-semi-massive PO,Py

 

Hole 12WA-23 was drilled to test a very strong conductivity anomaly possessing a 
coincident magnetic signature from Target Zone 2-4.  9 meters of overburden were 
encountered before entering intermediate volcanic rocks (quartz-garnet-anthrophyllite?-
biotite schists).  Intermediate volcanic flows(?) and intermediate breccias (quartz-phyric 
sericite schists) began at the overburden-bedrock interface  and dominate the lithologic 
units encountered for the remainder of the hole.  Semi-massive sulfides, dominated by 
pyrrhotite and lesser pyrite were encountered from 28.6 to 30.2 meters (1.6 meters).  
Present interpretation suggests this hole intercepted a distal facies of mineralization to a 
main VMS vent system at a stratigraphically equivalent position in the volcanic section.  
Mineralization encountered in this hole does not explain the strong conductor identified 
by the ground PEM survey.

Hole 12WA-24 was drilled to test a very strong conductivity anomaly possessing a

12WA-25 – Anomaly E 
Collar UTMN 5,728,078 EOH 149 metres
Collar UTME 524,924 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 315° Main Lithology Mafic volcanics with rhyolite

Dip at Collar -45° Main Mineralization PO, Py, ZnS, CuS, Ag

 

Hole 12WA-25 was designed to intercept the sulfide mineralization 50 meters above the 
zone intercepted in 2011 with drill hole 11WA-16.  12WA-25 was collared in mafic 
volcanic rocks.  The hole continued in altered mafic volcanic rocks to 110 meters at 
which point, quartz-phyric rhyolite was intersected.  Brecciated, fragmental dacitic-
rhyolitic volcanic rocks with chlorite alteration is present immediately above and 
throughout the mineralized interval. Massive and semi-massive pyrite, pyrrhotite with 
sphalerite and chalcopyrite were intersected from 99.6 meters to 115 meters (15.4 
meters).  Within this contiguous zone, silver averaged 16.1 ppm (0.50 opt Ag) with a 
high value of 61.1 ppm (1.91opt Ag) from 106-107m (1 meter).  The interval from 106 -
109m (3 meters) averages 47.7 ppm Ag (1.49 opt Ag).  
 
Within the same zone, 99.6 to 115 meters (15.4 meters), zinc averages 8,623 ppm 
(0.91% Zn) with an interval from 99.6 to 105m (5.4 meters) averaging 23,533 ppm zinc 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 71 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

(2.35% Zn). The high zinc value occurred from 102.5 to 103.5 meters (1 meter) and 
reported 76,000 ppm zinc (7.6% Zn). 
 
The 15.4 meter section also contains an average of 2,493 ppm (0.25% Cu) copper with 
a zone from 105 to 109m (4 meters) containing 6,568 ppm Copper.  From 106 to 108 
meters (2 meters), copper values average 10,395 ppm (1.4% Cu). The high copper 
value was from 106 to 107 meters (1 meter) at 11,550 ppm Cu (1.16% Cu). 
It appears that the rhyolite unit is the basal unit in the volcanic sequence at Anomaly E.  
Drilling of 12WA-25 was ended in the footwall granite at 149 meters. 
 

12WA-26 – Anomaly E 
Collar UTMN 5,728,005 EOH 252 metres
Collar UTME 524,096 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 315° Main Lithology Felsic Volcanics

Dip at Collar -50° Main Mineralization Py, PO, minor Ag

 

Hole 12WA-26 was designed to intercept the southwest continuation of the modeled 
Pulse EM conductor from the Crone ground survey at Anomaly E on Line 450(m) south.  
The intercept point on the longitudinal cross section penetrated the modeled plane 20 
meters above the depth of the conductor.  Only intense chlorite alteration and 
silicification with minor sulfides as disseminations and veins were noted in the core.  
Geochemical results also indicate only trace base metal contents in the mineralized 
(pyrite and pyrrhotite) zones encountered. 12WA-26 was collared in mafic volcanic 
rocks at 33 meters.  The hole continued in altered mafic volcanic rocks to 164.6 meters 
at which point, quartz-phyric rhyolite was intersected.  Brecciated, fragmental dacitic-
rhyolitic volcanic rocks with chlorite alteration is present throughout the felsic volcanic 
interval.  Within this zone, silver averaged 6.4 ppm (0.2 opt Ag) with a maximum value 
of 61.7 ppm (1.92opt Ag) from 199.5 to 200.5m (1 meter).  The interval from 197.6 – 
200.95m (3.35 meters) averages 45.7 ppm silver (1.63 opt Ag).  Within the same zone 
zinc and copper are elevated but not strongly anomalous. 
 
It appears that the rhyolite unit is the basal unit in the volcanic sequence at Anomaly E.  
Drilling of 12WA-26 was ended in the footwall granite at 252 meters. 
 

12WA-27 – Anomaly E 
Collar UTMN 5,728,103 EOH 224 metres
Collar UTME 525,051 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 312° Main Lithology Felsic Volcanics

Dip at Collar -50° Main Mineralization PO, Py, CuS, ZnS, Ag

 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 72 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

Hole 12WA-27 was designed to intercept the sulfide mineralization at Anomaly E, 80 
meters above the zone intercepted in 2011 with drill hole 11WA-17.  12WA-27 was 
collared in gabbro at -25.9 meters and entered altered mafic volcanic rocks at 27.6 
meters.  The hole continued in altered mafic volcanic rocks to 165.6 meters at which 
point, quartz-phyric rhyolite was intersected.  The mafic section contained thin (~ 
maximum 2 meter) dikes (sills?) of gabbro and quartz-feldspar porphyry.  Brecciated, 
fragmental dacitic-rhyolitic volcanic rocks with chlorite alteration are present 
immediately above and throughout the mineralized interval.  Massive, semi-massive 
and stringer zone pyrite, pyrrhotite with sphalerite and chalcopyrite were intersected 
from 169 meters to 211 meters (41 meters).  
 
Within this discontinuous zone (169 to 193.95 meters), silver averaged 10.9 ppm (0.31 
opt Ag) with a high value of 69.3 ppm (2.2 opt Ag) from 206 -207.15m (1.15 meters).  
The interval from 206 - 211m (5 meters) averages 37.4 ppm Ag (1.12 opt Ag).  
 
Within the same zone, 169 to 193.95 meters (24.95 meters), zinc averages 41,400 ppm 
(4.14% Zn).  From 181.9 to 182.9 (1 meter) zinc assays at 44,200 ppm (4.42% Zn).  
The high zinc values occur from 187.9 to 194 meters (6.1 meters) and averaged 
152,564 ppm (15.26% Zn), with an interval from 188.7 to 190.6 (1.9 meters) averaging 
382,300 ppm Zn (38.2% Zn).  
 
Within the 41 meter section, copper averages 3,068 ppm (0.31% Cu).  Over the 1 meter 
interval from 190.6 to 191.6 meters, copper assays at 19,950 ppm (1.995% Cu).  This is 
also the highest copper assay in this drill hole.  From 206 to 210 meters (4 meters) 
copper averages 11,178 ppm Cu (1.12% Cu).  Numerous other anomalous stringer 
zone analyses exist within the 41 meter interval.  
 
It appears that the rhyolite unit is the basal unit in the volcanic sequence at Anomaly E.  
Drilling of 12WA-27 was bottomed in the footwall rhyolite at 224 meters. 
 

12WA-28 – Anomaly E 
Collar UTMN 5,728,095 EOH 341 metres
Collar UTME 525,182 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 312° Main Lithology 

Dip at Collar -55° Main Mineralization 

 

Hole 12WA-28 was designed to intercept the sulfide mineralization at Anomaly E, 100 
meters above the zone intercepted in 2011 with drill hole 11WA-20.  12WA-28 was 
collared in an ultramafic rocks at -27 meters and entered altered mafic volcanics at 
169.8 meters.  The hole continued in altered mafic volcanic rocks to 207.1 meters at 
which point, quartz-phyric rhyolite was intersected.  The ultramafic and mafic sections 
contained thin (~ maximum 2 meter) dikes (sills?) of gabbro and quartz-feldspar 
porphyry.  Massive, fragmental and brecciated dacitic-rhyolitic volcanic rocks with 
chlorite alteration are present immediately above and throughout the mineralized 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 73 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

interval.  Chlorite-chalcopyrite+/-bornite stringers were intersected from 204.7 meters to 
300.7 meters (96 meters) along with disseminated chalcopyrite, pyrrhotite and pyrite.  
 
Within this continuous zone (204.7 to 300.7 meters), copper averaged 3,862 ppm (0.4 
% Cu) with a high value of 21,900ppm (2.2 % Cu) from 259.1to 260.1m (1 meter).  Nine 
additional one meter intervals (not contiguous) assayed over 1.2% copper.  Silver and 
zinc values from this drill hole are slightly elevated.  This 96 meter zone represents the 
widest intercept of stringer copper mineralization discovered to date at Anomaly E.  
 
It appears that the rhyolite unit is the basal unit in the volcanic sequence at Anomaly E.  
Drilling of 12WA-28 was bottomed in the footwall rhyolite at 341 meters. 
 

12WA-29 – A1 Zone 
Collar UTMN 5,733,002 EOH 74 metres
Collar UTME 525,620 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 220° Main Lithology Quartz Diorite & Mafic Volcanic

Dip at Collar -45° Main Mineralization Only trace amounts of chalcopyrite

 
Drill hole 12WA-29 was collared to attempt to test a very strong VTEM response 
(76,000 seimens) from the 2008 survey completed by Geotech over the Wabassi 
Intrusive Complex.  The hole penetrated 14.4 meters of overburden and collared in 
quartz diorite.  The hole continued through a mix of mafic volcanic rocks (quartz-biotite-
chlorite rock) and quartz diorite.  Only minor chalcopyrite was intercepted in this 74 
meter hole and did not explain the strong electromagnetic response.  From 14.4 to 16.4 
meters (2 meters), values averaged 0.198% copper.  From 60 to 61 meters (1 meter), 
copper values reported 0.15% and from 70 to 71 meters (1 meter), copper reported 
0.32%.  No other zones of anomalous sulfide mineralization were encountered.  
However, at approximately 27 meters, the azimuth of the planned hole (220 degrees) 
deviated radically to approximately 245 degrees, according to the down hole Reflex 
survey.  Additional drilling will be required to determine the source of this targeted EM 
response. 
 

12WA-30- A1 Zone 
Collar UTMN 5,733,191 EOH 236 metres
Collar UTME 525,454 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 110° Main Lithology 
Granite, Volcanic Breccia, 

Auriferous Quartz-Carbonate 
Shear Zone, Gabbro

Dip at Collar -60° Main Mineralization Pyrite, Gold

 

Hole 12WA-30 was also designed to test an airborne VTEM response from the 2008 
survey in addition to testing the predicted contact zone between the volcanic sequences 
and the Wabassi Intrusive Complex.  The hole was collared in granite after penetrating 
17.4 meters of overburden.  The hole intercepted heterolithic breccia from 130.94m 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 74 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

down to 157.99m, intermixed with thin gabbroic and pegmatitic dikes. Intense shearing 
and quartz veining parallel to shearing was encountered from 134.52-137.9m in a 
strongly silicified portion of the heterolithic breccia unit (3.4 meters).  From 157.99 to the 
end of the hole at 236m, the hole exhibited massive medium grained gabbronorite 
(Wabassi intrusive complex) intermixed with gabbroic and pegmatitic units, except for 
another interval of heterolithic breccia between 160.4-177.61m. 
 
Gold mineralization occurs in the 3.4 meter shear zone in the heterolithic breccias at 
130.94m, and averages 5.9 g/t Au (0.19 opt Au).  Within this 3.4 meter zone, a 1.03 
meter interval (135.52 to 136.55 meters) reported 16.3 g/t Au (0.51 opt Au). 
 
Additional drilling is planned for this target to further explore the shear zone-related gold 
mineralization as well as to determine the source of the EM conductor.

12WA-31 – A2 Zone 
Collar UTMN 5,732,480 EOH 149 metres
Collar UTME 525,376 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 110° Main Lithology Gabbronorite

Dip at Collar -80° Main Mineralization Trace Pyrrhotite

 

Drill hole 12WA-31 was set to test the northward continuation of the volcanic sequences 
containing VMS-style mineralization intercepted in drill holes 10WA-7 and 10WA-13.  
These host rocks and mineralization were drilled on the south end of a strong magnetic 
high anomaly.  Hole 12WA-31 was collared 100 meters to the north of hole 10WA-7 and 
angled to drill through the magnetic target.  After penetrating 11.8 meters of overburden, 
the hole collared in a gabbronorite.  This hole continued in gabbronorite to its 
termination at 149 meters, with the exception of a thin recrystallized breccia unit 
between 63.32-68.26m.  No mineralization of significance was encountered.  Additional 
drilling of the A2 Zone will focus on smaller step-outs from the ore intercepts to 
determine the geometry of the mineralization. 
 

12WA-32 – A2 Zone 
Collar UTMN 5,732,333 EOH 250 metres
Collar UTME 525,346 Dip of Layering Unknown 

Drilling Azimuth 290° Main Lithology Gabbronorite and Intrusive Breccia

Dip at Collar -60° Main Mineralization 
Pyrite, Pyrrhotite, Sphalerite, 

Chalcopyrite
 

Hole 12WA-32 was designed to test the southern extension of the proposed strike of the 
A2 mineralization found in holes 10WA-7 and 10WA-13.  It was collared 100 meters due 
south of hole 10WA-7 and drilled toward the west.  After penetrating 16 meters of 
overburden, the hole collared in gabbronorite.  This lithology continued throughout the 
entire whole.  However, from 56.5 to 114.5 meters (58 meters), an intrusive breccia was 
encountered.  This breccia consists of a gabbronorite matrix containing 0.5-3m clasts of 
ultramafic, mafic and felsic volcanic rocks.  Trace to anomalous pyrite, pyrrhotite, 
sphalerite and chalcopyrite mineralization was intercepted in three distinct zones within 
the breccia unit. Partially digested clasts of massive sphalerite with minor chalcopyrite 
were observed between 54.5-65.05m. 
 
From 56 to 59 meters (3 meters), zinc values averaged 1.21% Zn with a high value of 
3.2% from 56 to 57 meters (1 meter).  Within this same 3 meter interval, copper 
averaged 0.14%.  From 88.5 to 94.6 meters (6.1 meters), zinc averaged 0.2% and 
copper averaged 0.4%.  From 108.9 to 111.12 meters (2.22 meters), zinc averaged 
0.2%, copper averaged 0.42%. 
 
It is interpreted that this breccia unit, considering the volume of volcanic clasts 
contained within it, is part of the volcanic succession host to the VMS-style of 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 76 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

mineralization contained in the 2010 drill holes.  Additional work is planned to fill in 
drilling between these two locations and expand outward.  This hole was ended at 250 
meters.

Inc. 2012)

10.3 Franklin Geoscience Observations (on site core review, June, 2011) 
 
Discovery Harbour contracted Dr. James Franklin of Franklin Geoscience to review the 
core, downhole and assay data from the Property (Franklin 2011).  The holes examined 
included 10WA-07 and 13 from Anomaly A2 and 11WA-16, -17, -19 and -20 from 
Anomaly E.  The two anomalies are located approximately 4.2 kilometres apart (Figure 
11).  The summary of Franklins findings are: 
 

"1: Overall, the Wabassi area contains evidence of a robust VMS-
producing hydrothermal system. Although most of the mineralization 
intersected thus far is stringer type, there is some evidence, 
particularly at the Wabassi 'E" anomaly, that a conventional Noranda-
style VMS deposit may be present. Most VMS districts (Noranda, 
Matagami, Sturgeon Lake, Snow Lake, Flin Flon) contain a log-
normally sized set of deposits, with one giant (<20mt) deposit, one 
mid-sized (~10mt) deposit) and several smaller (2-4mt) deposits.  
 
2: A2 and E are about 4 km apart, a typical distance between 
hydrothermal centres in many VMS districts. In robust camps such as 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 81 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

those noted in (1) above, deposits are typically spaced evenly, at pre-
deformation distances of 3-5km. Although developing a local 
stratigraphic succession and geological map for this area will be 
challenging, consideration might be given to using the magnetic and 
other geophysical data to construct a geophysical-base map. This has 
been a successful approach in the Hudson's Bay Lowlands, for 
example  
 
3: The two zones explored thus far, A2 and E, are distinctly different in 
compositional and alteration attributes. A2 is enriched in Zn and Ag 
relative to Cu, and has some indications of Sturgeon Lake-style 
alteration. This may include some carbonate alteration (with Mn 
enrichment), which requires further examination. Wabassi A2 may 
have been partially assimilated by the adjacent mafic-ultramafic 
intrusion.  
 
4: The E zone is more clearly a high-temperature VMS system, similar 
to Noranda. Although the drilling does not seem to have intersected 
the core of this system, all of the alteration and compositional 
indicators indicate that it is proximal (within a few hundred meters) of a 
well-focused discharge zone.  

 
5: For both systems, Na depletion and Mg enrichment are the two most 
reliable alteration indicators. Use of the Mg/Na alteration index should 
be considered routinely as a guide to ore. Alteration distribution will be 
a more reliable indicator of stratigraphic polarity, relative to metal 
zoning.  

 
6: More petrochemical data should be collected to assist in determining 
the polarity of the system, as well as the scale of alteration. Additional 
WR analyses outside of the mineralized zones are needed to better 
determine the stratigraphic polarity. Alteration tends to diminish 
gradually into the footwall, but stop sharply at the ore horizon. A WR 
sample every 25 m, or where there is a lithology change, should be 
taken." (Franklin 2011)." 

 
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 82 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

11.0 SAMPLE PREPARATION, ANALYSIS AND SECURITY 
 
Core was logged for lithology, mineralization, and alteration.  The drill core samples 
were cut, and measured samples were bagged with a numerical assay tag and stapled 
shut under the supervision of the geologist onsite.  The responsible geologist's name is 
listed on the relevant core log.  All core was photographed prior to sampling.  The 
sampling was done using a diamond saw and the sample length was loosely 
standardized to one metre with breaks at lithological and mineralogical contacts.  
Standard samples and blanks were inserted approximately every 20 samples submitted 
for assay.  A program for duplicate samples has not been initiated at this time, though 
un-sampled core is available for such a program.   
  
The QA/QC results were gathered and collated by Northern Shield. Blanks and 
standards were compared with the nominated values and acceptable error limits.  For 
blanks, all values returned were very low and there were no failures.  For standards 
there were no failures. 
 
Sample selection has dominantly occurred at the project camps (Highbank Lake for 
programs up to 2011, Mink Lake camp for 2012 drilling).  Drill core has largely been re-
located to the float-plane airbase at Hearst Air, Hearst, ON.  Mineralized intervals are 
stored in lock-secured truck and shipping containers.  Un-mineralised / un-altered core 
is stacked at the remote Highbank Lake and Mink Lake camps. 
  
All samples were sent to ALS Minerals laboratory in Timmins, Ontario for preparation.  
Samples are submitted using the standard ALS Sample Submittal Form with sample 
chain of custody following standard ALS Group procedures.  ALS Minerals is a division 
of the ALS Group and each of ALS Minerals laboratories in North America are 
registered to ISO 9001:2008 for the "provision of assay and geochemical analytical 
services" by QMI Quality Registrars.  The North America analytical laboratories are also 
accredited by the Standards Council of Canada (SCC) for specific tests listed in their 
Scope of Accreditation No. 579, http://palcan.scc.ca/specs/pdf/677_e.pdf.  This 
accreditation is based on ISO 17025:2005 international standards and involves 
extensive site audits and performance evaluations. 
  
The ALS Group companies are independent of, and unrelated to each and any of 
Discovery Harbour Resources, CVC Cayman Ventures and Northern Shield Resources. 
  
All analyses were completed using industry standard methods. Analysis completed 
utilized ALS Minerals process codes PGM-MS23 for platinum, palladium and gold, ME-
MS81 for a 38 element trace element package and ME-ICP61 for a 33 element trace 
element package. 
  
Sample Preparation Package PREP-31 is a standard sample preparation for analysis 
that involves the following steps: Dry, Crush, Split and Pulverize.  The sample is logged 
in the tracking system, weighed, dried and finely crushed to better than 70 % (generally 
75%) passing a 2 mm (Tyler 9 mesh, US Std. No.10) screen.  A split of up to 250 grams 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 83 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

is taken and pulverized to better than 85 % passing a 75 micron (µ)(Tyler 200 mesh, US 
Std. No. 200) screen. 
  
PGM-MS23 is a Pt, Pd, Au package that uses a 30gram sample fire assay with 
detection by Inductively Coupled Plasma - Mass Spectroscopy (ICP - MS).  The sample 
is fused with a mixture of lead oxide, sodium carbonate, borax and silica inquarted with 
6 mg of gold-free silver and then cupelled to yield a precious metal bead.  The bead is 
digested at high power by microwave in dilute nitric acid.  The solution is cooled and 
hydrochloric acid is added.  The solution is then digested at half power by microwave.  
The digested solution is then cooled, diluted with hydrochloric acid, homogenized and 
then analyzed for gold, platinum and palladium by ICP-MS analysis. 
 
Geochemical Procedure ME- MS81 is an ultra- trace level analytical technique using 
specialized sample decomposition by lithium metaborate fusion (FUS-LI01) with 
detection by Inductively Coupled Plasma - Mass Spectroscopy (ICP - MS).  A prepared 
sample (0.200 g) is added to lithium metaborate flux (0.90 g), mixed well and fused in a 
furnace at 1000°C.  The resulting melt is then cooled and dissolved in 100 mL of 4% 
HNO3 / 2% HCl3 solution.  This solution is then analyzed by ICP - MS. 
  
Geochemical Procedure ME- ICP61 is a trace level analytical method using a four-acid 
sample digestion and HCl Leach (GEO -4ACID) with detection by conventional 
Inductively Coupled Plasma - Atomic Emission Spectroscopy (ICP - AES).  A prepared 
sample (0.25 g) is digested with perchloric, nitric, hydrofluoric and hydrochloric acids.  
The residue is topped up with dilute hydrochloric acid and the resulting solution is 
analyzed by ICP - AES.  Results are corrected for spectral inter-element interferences. 
  
For major oxides and loss on ignition (LOI) determination, pulped samples were fused 
with lithium borate to produce a glass disk, which was then analyzed by X-ray 
fluorescence spectrometry.  The major elements in the complete characterization 
package were done by fusion with ICP-AES finish. 
  
Sulphur and carbon concentrations were determined using the Leco method. 
  
All certificates of analysis for samples processed for assay and for whole-rock 
lithogeochemistry are filed at the Northern Shield offices, and duplicate copies can be 
obtained from ALS Minerals laboratories. 
  
All steps of the sample selection and transportation to the laboratory were supervised 
and monitored by Northern Shield personelle. 
  
It is the author's opinion that that: 
• sufficient care was applied to ensure the integrity of the samples during collection 
and processing and that the chain of custody applied to samples is appropriate for the 
Wabassi project, and that 
• the sample preparation and analytical / assay methods selected are appropriate 
for the mineralization encountered, and 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 84 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

• the author reviewed the sampled intervals and considers the sampling to have 
been done properly, in a manner appropriate for the deposit type and mineralization 
style, and that 
• the analytical data generated by ALS Minerals Laboratories is reliable and 
sufficiently precise and accurate for the purpose of the Technical report.

25.0 INTERPRETATION AND CONCLUSIONS 
 
Exploration completed prior to the 2010 diamond drill program was focused on 
evaluating the potential of the Wabassi Intrusive complex to host Ni-Cu-PGE.  A strong 
mix of economic and academic geological principals and theory was used coupled with 
modern geophysics to define excellent diamond drill targets.  The early exploration 
completed on the Property focused on the discovery of Ni-Cu-PGE mineralization. The 
evaluation of conductive zones has succeeded on highlighting the VMS potential of the 
property and further exploration will focus on this potential. 
 
The 2008 and 2010 VTEM airborne geophysical programs have defined a series of 
conductors that were tested with the 2010 and 2011 diamond drill program (20 diamond 
drill holes – 5250 metres). These diamond drill holes tested airborne anomalies A1, A2, 
B, C, D, and E.  2012 drilling (12 holes totaling 2,046m) tested two regional targets 
(Anomalies 2-4 and 2-9), and further tested targets within the A1, A2 and E Zones.  The 
most significant results were attained at A2 and E that revealed the presence of Zn-Cu-
Ag-(Au) volcanogenic massive sulphide (VMS) mineralization in the metavolcanic rocks 
at the margins of the Wabassi Intrusive complex.  Shear zone hosted auriferous quartz-
carbonate veining was discovered in the A1 Zone during the 2012 summer drilling 
program (hole 12WA-30).  Due to the lack of outcrop and the success of targeting VMS 
mineralization using geophysics, future targeting of diamond drilling would best be 
guided by geophysical surveys and diamond drill hole visual and geochemical 
observations. 
 
A review of the geophysical data by Condor Geophysics has modelled the anomalies 
revealing excellent potential for expansion of the intersected mineralization. 
 
A review of drill core, collar and downhole data and assay data from the Property was 
completed by Franklin Geoscience.  Observations concluded that the Wabassi area 
contains evidence of a robust VMS-producing hydrothermal system similar to that of the 
Sturgeon Lake-style alteration and Anomaly E represents VMS mineralization 
potentially similar to the high-temperature Noranda-style VMS mineralization.  
 
The exploration information relied on for this project is all modern and has been 
managed by qualified persons.  Therefore there are no significant risks or uncertainties 
progressing forward with continued exploration. 
 
The author believes that the Wabassi property requires additional exploration to 
evaluate the potential of hosting economic VMS and shear zone-hosted gold 
mineralization.   
  



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 87 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

26.0 RECOMMENDATIONS 
 
In light of the results obtained in the exploration work described in this Technical Report, 
recommendations for a work program are focused on follow-up work in Zones A and E 
as described below and on new targets generated from the recently completed airborne 
VTEM survey over the expanded Wabassi property. Estimated costs for each element 
of the recommended exploration programs are provided in Table 3-18.1.  
 
Recommendations for the A1 Zone. 
 
In the A1 Zone, it is recommended to: 

1. diamond drill test the gold bearing shear zone by designing intercept points 
above and below the point of gold mineralization  Recommend 2 holes, 200 
meter total. 
 

In the E Zone it is recommended to: 
1) Complete a minimum of two additional drill-holes to further define the VMS 

occurrence along strike and at depth.  1,000 meter total 
Considering the quality of many of the regional targets defined with the 2011 VTEM 
survey, it is further recommended to drill test a minimum of two of the high priority 
regional targets discovered from this survey.  550 meter total. 
  

Table 3: Estimated cost of recommended exploration program.  Based on an all-in cost of $400.00 per meter 
of drilling. 

Work Program Estimated Cost 
 
A1 Zone Drilling – 200 meters 
 

 
$80,000.00 
 

 
E Zone Drilling – 1,000 meters 
 

 
$400,000.00 
 

 
Regional Target Drilling – 550 meters 
 

 
$220,000.00 
 

Total (51% Discovery Harbour = $357,000; 49% NRN = $343,000) $700,000 
 
 
A CDN $700,000.00 exploration budget is recommended to further assess the Wabassi 
Property for Volcanogenic massive sulphides and gold mineralization.  This exploration 
program is projected to span 12-14 months. 
 
Additional work programs and budgets will obviously be contingent on the results 
from this phase of exploration and because of this variable, any attempt to define 
objectives and specifics, regarding future activity and cost, would be speculative. It is 
the opinion of the author that the property is of sufficient merit to justify this proposed 
exploration. 



Discovery Harbour Resources  Wabassi Property 

November 2012 88 Clark Expl. Consulting Inc. 

 
The work completed to date has relied on quality geophysical surveys to allow the 
Discovery and Northern Shield geologists and their consultants to interpret the 
dominantly covered geology.  The success to date has proven the potential for 
significant volcanogenic massive sulphides (VMS) mineralization. 
 
The 2011 VTEM survey requires a detailed interpretation consisting of EM anomaly 
picking, resistivity depth imaging, plan resistivity depth slices and modelling of targets 
for drill testing solutions.   
 
All data from the drilling and geophysics should be incorporated into a modelling system 
that will help direct the future projects. 
 
It is recommended that the company continue to enact a solid a QA/QC program for all 
future drilling.  This program should include but not be limited to insertion of a blanks 
and standards protocol in the sampling process. 
 

*Note: This proposed budget will not support the testing of all known targets on 
the joint venture's claims blocks but will enable the further testing of the two 
proven discoveries as well as the priority VTEM targets as understood to-date 
and further refined through geophysical modeling. Detailed ground geophysical 
follow-up of these untested targets will assist in the prioritization of the zones for 
drill testing.
